commit c3dd918c22d880f408d219139fb1792caa588990
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Feb 29 22:54:00 2020 +0100

    ScaledInt: Improve accuracy of operators, fix enum type issues.
    
    Multiplication and division now call one of the static mulDiv functions directly instead of first converting the operand with the smaller scale to the larger scale. This leads to more accurate results and may also be faster.
    
    The comparison operators now convert both operands to the product of the two scales (unless the scales are the same), using 64 bit if necessary. This makes comparisons exact - as they should be.
    
    My approach to the EnumType parameter -- defining function templates only for matching types -- doesn't work after all; at least not so easily. For now, matching types are enforced by static assertions.
    
    And I've renamed "scaled_int" to "scaled" and "scaled_uint" to "uscaled". The default scale factor is now 2048. The class template is still named ScaledInt.

commit ca9bcfb831e2d1fd363bcc2f5af3ae43d264fa83
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Feb 22 22:21:57 2020 +0100

    More work on ScaledInt (to be continued)
    
    Introduce a single mulDiv member function for all multiplications by a ratio; replacing the toScale function.
    The global arithmetic operators with two ScaledInt operands are now templates that can accept operands on different scales and of different integer types.
    New header TypeChoice.h to allow the functions above to choose their return types based on the operand types.
    
    safeCast function for casts to IntType added.
    
    Workaround for friend bug in MSVC03: Set the scale factor through an int parameter iSCALE; cast iSCALE into a static IntType const member SCALE.
    
    Assertions to detect overflow when rounding to nearest in ScaledInt::round. Open issue: For unsigned IntType, overflow could also occur when rounding in ScaledInt::mulDiv – and would currently go unnoticed.
    
    Remove increasedTo and decreasedTo const functions.
    Remove fromRational<int>(int) -- use ScaledInt(int,int) instead.

commit 11d0b2e88af90990389dc4b15f1cea5951fc652c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Feb 19 23:08:17 2020 +0100

    Revise ScaledInt class (to be continued)
    
    Prompted by comments by Nightinggale and devolution in this CFC thread:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/class-for-fixed-point-arithmetic.655037/
    (But not all comments have been addressed yet.)
    
    Turn static ScaledInt::szBuf from a char array into a CvString and move it to a base class because one instance shared by all ScaledInt types is enough.
    
    Rename static variables MIN and MAX to INTMIN, INTMAX to make clearer that they're the limits of IntType, not of ScaledInt. Now private. Add public functions MIN(), MAX() that return the limits of ScaledInt based on INTMIN and INTMAX.
    
    Changes to template parameters:
    * Replace 'class' with 'typename' in template parameter lists.
    * Rename the 'INT' parameter to 'IntType', in part, because INT is already defined (as an alias of int) in WinDef.h.
    * Switch the order of SCALE and IntType so that SCALE can be of type IntType. Known issue with this: Can't declare template classes with dependent arguments as friend; this appears to be a bug in the MSVC compiler:
    https://stackoverflow.com/questions/18666240/friending-a-dependent-argument-template
    I've made all private data members public until I can find a workaround.
    * Add a template parameter 'EnumType' to allow instantiations that are (on purpose; for type safety) incompatible with each other.
    * Remove unnecessary template argument lists.
    * Use preprocessor defines to make parameter/ argument lists easier to handle in global and out-of-class definitions.
    
    Define a type LongType depending on the size of IntType for intermediate results that are outside the limits of IntType. (Previously, __int64 was always used, which is wasteful when IntType has fewer than 4 bytes.)
    
    Add some more assertions to check for overflow and signed/unsigned mismatches.
    
    Add uint comparison operators. (Tbd.: Try using function templates instead.)
    
    Add serialization functions that read and write to FDataStreamBase.
    
    Fix an overflow bug in operator/= by forwarding to the toScale function.
    In the works: A mulDiv function template to handle operator*=, operator/= and scale conversions. Currently, there is some duplicate code, and operations on mixed scales aren't as accurate as they could be.

commit 8f753f67c2a0faa5974fd3890c11979e7d7a06cb
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Feb 12 16:44:24 2020 +0100

    Treat NoWarProb of Random Pers. as secret; map trade speed tweak.
    
    The AI now treats the NoWarProb values of other AI leaders as secret when playing with Random Personalities. [advc.104y]
    
    When trying to even out an AI-AI tech trade, maps are only considered when they have a significant trade value. [advc.136b]
    This was intended as a performance tweak, but it turns out that by far the slowest part of a map trade is the graphics update – and that occurs only when the active human player is involved. Specifically, the update of route graphics is very slow; it seems that the game core DLL can't do anything about that.
    
    And some misc. refactoring.

commit c16d688b14839d095beefc52209b3a74decf2364
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Feb 4 22:56:03 2020 +0100

    Class scaled_int for fixed-point math incl. pow function
    
    [change id advc.fract]
    
    Some initial tests for correctness and speed look promising. Seems like scaled_int won't be significantly slower or faster than double (nor did I expect it to be faster). Not sure that I've overloaded all the right operators. Perhaps I'll switch to using boost/operators.hpp later.
    
    The power function (for fractions) could surely be improved in terms of accuracy and speed, but, for my needs, the current implementation may well be sufficient.
    
    I don't think I'll convert all my floating-point code to scaled_int, or at least not the UWAI component. The interface of scaled_int is intended to be rich enough though to make that conversion feasible if necessary.
    
    I intend to use scaled_int in modified BtS code in order to make my changes portable to mods that don't use floating-point numbers. ScaledInt.h itself should be pretty easily portable.
    (But I won't change the rounding behavior in places that players can and do observe, e.g. +25% from Forge will continue to amount to 0 when the city's base production rate is less than 4.)
    
    Ties in with this "We the People" issue (and #169):
    https://github.com/We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod/issues/176

commit 206f9c6a96fdafc1985b34e304438327304082be
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 24 16:01:55 2020 +0100

    Merge FLTA class with its base; resolve type cast problems.
    
    [change id 003u]
    
    Removed the unused FFreeListArray class. That left only FFreeListTrashArray (short: FLTA) and its base class FFreeListArrayBase. I've merged them into a single class to facilitate further changes.
    
    Moved all FLTA code that calls member functions of the template argument from the FLTA header file into an implementation file and added explicit instantiations. This way, client code can call the iteration functions (beginIter, nextIter, getAt) without having to include the headers that define the template argument. In that same vein, FLTA now has an optional second template parameter for a base class type and can return pointers to that base class type. For example, FLTA<CvUnit,CvUnitAI>::getAt returns a CvUnit* and AI_getAt a CvUnitAI*.

commit f0551b743bd82d3c92fbf1ea405a566ef3d2e6b8
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jan 22 22:38:16 2020 +0100

    Inlined getUnit(IDInfo), getCity(IDInfo)
    
    IDInfo structs that represent no city or no unit now store the id of the Barbarian player instead of NO_PLAYER. The FreeList id is set to FFreeList::INVALID_INDEX as before. This change makes the NO_PLAYER check in getUnit and getCity (and AI_getUnit, AI_getCity) unnecessary and makes it worth inlining those functions. I've moved them from CvGameCoreUtils to CvPlayer(AI).h (still as global functions) for that purpose - CvGameCoreUtils.h doesn't (and shouldn't) include CvPlayer.h. For files that need to call getCity or getUnit, don't include CvPlayer.h and don't care much about performance, I've added static wrapper functions named "fromIDInfo" to CvCity, CvCityAI, CvUnit and CvUnitAI.
    
    Also removed an unnecessary NULL check from FreeListTrashArray::getAt.

commit 09ea6a2887242534b481c854f4807faac12af2fc
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 17 02:37:34 2020 +0100

    Adjust/ fix decay probabilities of AI diplo memory counters
    
    Changed the formula for faster decay when multiple diplo actions are remembered. For example, two declarations of war should now be fully forgotten after an expected duration of 150+75 turns on Normal speed. Three declarations after 150+75+50 turns. Etc. My old formula was ... more complicated and incorrectly implemented. [advc.130r]
    
    Memory about tech trades ("you're becoming too advanced", "you shared your discoveries") are exempt from the above, i.e. they decay as in BtS with a per-turn probability that doesn't depend on the memory count. However, for "you shared your discoveries", I've increased the per-turn probability by a factor of 4, meaning that one tech is forgotten, on average, every 25 turns instead of every 100 turns. The relations modifier per tech is now between 0.08 and 0.2 (was between 0.05 and 0.2) and fractions get rounded to the nearest integer. (The rounding change is not part of this commit; has been in place since v0.8 or so. BtS rounds down.) On the bottom line, +1 from shared discoveries should be easier to get than in BtS, but more difficult to sustain. (Not sure about higher modifiers.) Still to be tested. [advc.553]
    
    "You gave us help" now decays with a (base) probability of 1/150; was 1/200. [advc.144]

commit de7f9344698fe504740b11a6864b454821347a51
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Jan 16 19:48:20 2020 +0100

    Performance tweaks: plotDanger, isEnemy
    
    Merged CvPlayerAI::AI_getPlotDanger and AI_getAnyPlotDanger into a single function and made various small performance tweaks.
    
    Overloaded CvUnit::isEnemy(TeamTypes,CvPlot const*) so that the original function doesn't have to check whether for NO_TEAM and NULL. isEnemy is checked extremely frequently, but, since always-hostile units (Privateers) have to be supported, there isn't much one can do to make it faster.
    
    At a few call locations of isEnemy, I've changed call parameters because the original parameters didn't quite make sense to me. Those changes should only be relevant when a mod-mod gives the always-hostile ability to additional units.
    
    Renamed or replaced a bunch of functions:
    CvPlayerAI::AI_getAnyPlotDanger -> AI_isAnyPlotDanger
    CvUnit::isPotentialEnemy -> CvUnitAI::AI_isPotentialEnemyOf
    CvUnit::potentialWarAction -> CvUnitAI::AI_mayAttack(CvPlot const&)
    CvUnitAI::AI_potentialEnemy -> CvUnitAI::AI_mayAttack(TeamTypes,CvPlot const&)
    isPotentialEnemy (CvGameCoreUtils) -> CvTeamAI::AI_mayAttack(TeamTypes)
    CvPlot::isVisiblePotentialEnemyUnit -> CvTeamAI::AI_mayAttack(CvPlot const&)
    CvPlot::getNumVisiblePotentialEnemyDefenders -> CvUnitAI::AI_countEnemyDefenders/ AI_isAnyEnemyDefender
    CvSelectionGroup::isHasPathToAreaEnemyCity -> CvSelectionGroupAI::AI_isHasPathToAreaEnemyCity
    
    CvUnit now uses EnumMaps. CvUnit.h includes CvInfo_Unit.h so that the forwarding functions can be inlined.

            for k in range(gc.getNumFeatureInfos()):

commit 279c9d078008359b9fa4680e1146c35c68f345cc
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Jan 4 17:23:25 2020 +0100

    Tweaks to AI code for automated air recon
    
    [change id advc.029]
    
    Consider the full recon range around each candidate target; BBAI had only looked at the adjacent tiles.
    
    Non-visible water tiles aren't preferred. (It seems that the BBAI code was mainly intended for spotting incoming transports.) Prefer exploration near non-friendly tiles and especially near enemy tiles instead. (I expect that exploration on water will still be the most common result; there tend to be a lot of non-visible water tiles.)
    
    Don't prefer to target tiles at maximal range.

commit 70b59ebcbd6f9dd0d1e1069cfcae537b9a8e14d2
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Jan 4 15:05:23 2020 +0100

    Fix BBAI bugs in automated air recon
    
    In the code that selects the recon target tile, a visibility check was flipped. As a result, the target was chosen randomly with a bias only for maximal distance from the airbase.
    
    Also, tiles around the airbase had been evaluated instead of tiles around the candidate recon tile.
    
    BBAI uses its AI air recon function only for automated human units, but change [advc.650] also lets the AI use it.
    
    Even with the bugs fixed, it's not a good heuristic. I'll make some tweaks in a separate commit.

commit 968ae050e022c151a53562e962ffcd3c03c65f19

commit b96465d167c7fa35f0a8d974eccd457d9dcb7edb
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 3 02:18:48 2020 +0100

    Refactor CvArea getter functions
    
    Changed CvArea function parameters from CvArea* and (occasionally) int to CvArea const& when possible. Repurposed the getArea functions (CvPlot, CvCity, CvUnit) to return a CvArea&. Same-area checks are now usually performed by functions 'sameArea', e.g. CvCity::sameArea(CvCity const&), or isArea(CvArea const&). The 'area' functions (CvPlot, CvCity, CvUnit, CvSelectionGroup) aren't used much anymore, but are retained for compatibility with other DLL mods. (The change to the getArea functions will hurt compatibility though.) All functions mentioned above are inlined except CvSelectionGroup::area. Previously, most of them weren't inlined because CvPlot and CvArea objects had to be looked up in CvMap. Now CvPlot, CvCity and CvUnit each store a CvArea*, and CvPlot no longer stores an area id.
    (The 'plot' functions still aren't inlined; same problem. Also the 'getTeam' functions.)
    
    And I've inlined some CvUnit getter functions.

commit 9f296435d19adf72f15a4bc2f0ccec1c70982b88
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Dec 30 00:52:01 2019 +0100

    Update player AI cache data after loading savegame
    
    The cache in question contains some misc. CvPlayerAI data and was introduced by K-Mod. Updating the cache after loading means that the cache data don't necessarily have to be serialized. The cache normally gets updated at the start of a player's turn. That means, only the cache of the active human player didn't get updated after loading. The human cache matters for testing through AI Auto Play, so, for development purposes this is an important bugfix. (All the K-Mod cache data was being serialized, so the error had been mine alone.)

commit 8a3cf7d4606d71b4dc5cca74a7103ff24f7c7355
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Dec 28 22:49:03 2019 +0100

    AI may pay for peace even if it thinks that both sides want it
    
    (UWAI component)
    
    Previously, an AI civ had never paid a human player for peace if it thought that peace was in both sides' interest. Now the AI will pay based on the difference between AI peace utility and two times the human peace utility. (It won't pay if that difference isn't positive.)
    
    Thanks to everyone on the CFC forums who had complained about the old behavior. It was too reliant on what the AI "thought" about the human player's situation, and it's not a reasonable position to insist on a square peace treaty when continuing the war is disastrous for one side and merely inconvenient for the other.
    
    The AI is now also a bit more generous when paying for peace in situations when the war is going badly but not extremely badly. (For extremely bad wars, the AI still assumes that peace is unlikely to last and therefore not worth very much.)

commit fb1794179682ba78647f63ea54fe6b2870b6a08c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Dec 26 22:30:02 2019 +0100

    Change culture garrison strength formula; add tooltip.
    
    Culture garrison strength is now equal to current combat strength with the following modifiers:
    - Defensive modifiers (Archery units, Garrison promotions)
    - Generic strength modifiers (Combat promotions)
    - Minus 50% for non-lethal units (i.e. Siege except Machine Gun).
    iCultureGarrison in XML is obsolete.
    
    Adjusted the foreign culture strength formula to balance out the change to culture garrison strength, and to make revolts a bit easier to suppress in the midgame and a bit harder in the late game. Added two XML parameters for fine-tuning this.
    
    Added hover text on the main map and city screen (nationality bar) showing how much more garrison strength is needed to reduce a city's revolt chance to 0, or how much garrison strength can be safely removed.

commit 4d0dc0f4fa1e90103f76e6134d4d267659d10c67

    Allow air unit production in cities with insufficient capacity
    
    [change id advc.001b]
    
    Basically back to how it worked in BtS. The AdvCiv rule can still be enabled through GlobalDefines_advc.xml.
    
    Unlike in BtS, units that are force-moved upon completion have their movement points spent. When a (legal) rally point is set, force-moved units are sent there. When no rally point is set, units are moved to the nearest legal city or fort (or destroyed if there is none) as in BtS and a message is shown on the main interface.

commit 891273d300ade2b2adc69bb9cc0a907c74e59267
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Dec 21 13:19:32 2019 +0100

    AI city placement tweaks
    
    [change id advc.031]
    
    Some special discouragement from settling on top of a (high-yield) resource is needed after all. And fixed various other issues introduced recently when moving/ refactoring the city site evaluation code, including crashes on flat maps.
    
    The tech checks and yield computation for resources were still incorrect in several ways.
    
    Made the placement of the second AI city less strategic (i.e. less about preempting a neighbor) and thus more focused on tile yields etc.
    
    Resources on tiles that the AI hopes to flip are no longer ignored.
    
    Adjustments to resource trade values, especially in the early game.
    
    No Lighthouse food assumed when settling in a non-coastal tile.
    
    The food modifier computed from resource yields no longer applies to non-resource tiles.
    
    Reduced the impact of the general low-food modifier.
    
    Stricter bad-health check to discourage early Jungle cities.
    
    Chopping yield is no longer assumed for features that probably shouldn't be chopped (Tundra Forests).
    
    Account for features that don't allow improvements (Oasis).
    
    Distance penalties reduced.
    
    Fixed a small issue with the detection of deadlocked resources that had sometimes discouraged the AI from colonizing an island chain.
    
    City placement in Advanced Start assumes that borders are easy to expand.
    
    Various adjustments to culture modifiers for contested tiles.
    
    Various small tweaks.
    
    AI exploration units now prioritize the surroundings of (tentative) city sites. [advc.031d]

commit 078fc9bd7c7962bdd944073c372ffd2e5853b16e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Dec 15 23:33:35 2019 +0100

    Move AI_foundValue computation into a new class
    
    Also split the code into subroutines. This has mandated -or strongly suggested- other refactoring changes to the found value code.
    
    I've taken this opportunity to add logging code. When the log is enabled through BBAILog.h, a breakdown of the found value computation is written to the BBAI log file whenever an AI player founds a city and when placing or normalizing a starting location. When an AI city is founded, breakdowns are also written for the found value of the best adjacent tile and for the next best city site overall. [advc.031c]
    
    The few logs I've looked at and the refactoring changes have brought to light or reminded me of some minor issues, which I've fixed: [advc.031]
    * Improved evaluation of chopping (was previously factored into the health evaluation).
    * Revised tech requirement checks for resources (techs for revealing, improving, trading the resource).
    * Removed a K-Mod kludge (negative yields assumed on the city tile) that was supposed to discourage the AI from settling on top of resources and flood plains. Hopefully no longer needed.
    * Disabled K-Mod code that was supposed to steer the distribution of starting locations among landmasses. As far as I can tell, CvPlayer::findStartingArea handles that.
    * Made the AI more pessimistic about flipping tiles near a colony on a continent where a rival already has multiple cities.
    (Thanks to keldath for making me aware of that potential problem a while ago.)
    * Don't count on getting the upper hand culturally when both sides have the Creative trait.
    * Disabled some minor (probably inadvertent) visibility cheats.
    * Made the AI reluctant to move its starting Settler more than 1 tile on maps with a higher-than-normal player count (e.g. more than 8 on a Standard-size map with Medium sea level). To make situations like the one reported here by Elkad
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-22#post-15602780
    more unlikely. [advc.108]
    * Slightly increased production yield weight for Barbarian cities (no bias previously). [advc.303]
    * Some tweaks in the evaluation of sea access.
    * Minor bugfix: AI personality had sometimes affected city site evaluation when computing recommendations for humans and when placing starting locations.
    
    Only tangentially related:
    Choosing the "Balanced resources" map option now causes more aggressive normalization of starting locations. In particular, unrevealed resources are then taken into account. [advc.108]

commit b2b7802dd311c71630e9c2fad45e750ed2d93114

    Field-of-view slider tweaks
    
    [change id advc.090]
    
    Slightly longer bar (at least on high resolutions), which makes it a bit easier to set the slider to a particular value. However, the issue described here (at the end of the post)

commit d69859907a71e062be91500b529701e0d22d5c39
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Dec 11 23:53:43 2019 +0100

    Options for replay minimap texture
    
    When the HOF_STORE_REPLAYS_AS_BTS option is not enabled, then replay files store the MINIMAP_RENDER_SIZE value that was used to generate the terrain texture. This allows players to change the texture resolution without breaking compatibility. [advc.106m]
    
    REPLAY_TEXTURE_ERA option in XML that allows storing a terrain texture for the replay file before the game is over so that the replay minimap doesn't reflect e.g. terrain changes from global warming. [advc.106n]
    
    See GlobalDefines_advc.xml for more info about these two changes (updated manual yet to be committed). There are also related posts in the AdvCiv thread on CFC:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-24#post-15610743
    
    The column with the "start replay" buttons is hidden when the Hall of Fame screen is entered at the end of a game. (Replays can't be viewed at that point; the buttons had no effect.) [advc.106i]
    
    Increased initial camera distance a bit. [advc.004m]
    (Seems to be affected by the screen resolution; I guess most players use Full HD by now.)
    
    And some rather minor refactoring in CvReplayInfo.cpp.

commit 6029d4205ce0e3c6206d816ee2d8b9a6c46442d5
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Nov 15 16:07:26 2019 +0100

    AgentIterator class for looping over players and teams
    
    [change id advc.agent]
    
    I'm using "agent" as a generic term for player or team.
    
    E.g. for looping over all major (non-minor, non-Barbarian) teams alive, one can write:
    for (TeamIter it(MAJOR_CIV); it.hasNext(); ++it)
    {
       CvTeam& kTeam = *it;
       // ...
    }
    
    I'm happy with this interface, but, although the major teams alive are cached, it's slightly slower than the BtS code, even when only 8 out of 48 teams are alive. The iterator is already pretty extensively optimized, so I may have to try turning the constructor arguments into template arguments (not so nice):
    TeamIter<MAJOR_CIV> it()
    
    Also, the cache updates (CvAgents.h/cpp) haven't really been tested yet.

commit f88b62c0d397a3be6ec4cbaab36f40efc81cb487
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 9 11:29:44 2019 +0100

    Don't require RandLog for OOSLog
    
    Only MessageLog=1 is required now. When debugging OOS errors, RandLog=1 should normally be set, but when playing for the sake of playing, RandLog writes too much data. The MessageLog requirement is somewhat important though because the OOS log will contain hidden parts of the game state and MessageLog=1 makes sure that players are aware of that by showing a "logging enabled" popup on the Staging Room screen.
    
    [change id dlph.27]

commit b513eb97b484d6fd5741aedc2a01689cb9184a64

    No Barbarian target city when no Barbarian cities in area

    Barbarian city attackers ignore the target city when deciding which city to move toward – unless there is a Barbarian city on the same landmass. [advc.300]

    Can choose between TSC Profiler and Firaxis's DLL-internal profiler through Makefile.project. FP_PROFILE_ENABLE is now implied by USE_INTERNAL_PROFILER. [advc.make]
    
    Unrelated [advc.make]: Use the Ob1 compiler flag to allow some inline expansion in debug builds. In a single test, this reduced AI turn times by 30% when debugging.
    And allow compiler flags for debug builds to be set through Makefile.project.

commit 19fbdb93ab129070eac82fcfde79334a1ddac29e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Nov 3 22:04:32 2019 +0100

    Fix spurious "can no longer work on" popups
    
    When updating all plot groups during the active player's turn, e.g. after discovering Sailing through a tech trade, it was possible that cities producing an order with a resource requirement were interrupted.
    
    The problem was introduced with [advc.064d] (blocks an exploit for storing arbitrary amounts of overflow production), so I think it can occur in the v0.96 releases; hopefully only rarely.
    
    The new code should also be a little faster because it no longer checks for maxed out wonders when plot groups are updated.
    
    (And a few misc. style changes.)

commit 031cc06cb2cf73b6ae824c08d7021a72ec6e2c9e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Oct 30 03:26:28 2019 +0100

    Don't check array bounds when looping over all plots
    
    Replaced most calls to CvMap::plotByIndex with a new function getPlotByIndex, which returns a CvPlot reference and doesn't check array bounds. When looping over all plots on the map (from index 0 to CvMap::numPlots()), there is no danger of going out of bounds. Some of those loops are relevant for overall performance, so it's nice to get rid of unnecessary branching.
    
    As a side-effect, most of the loops over all plots now use CvPlot references, and, to accommodate that, I've changed the signatures of some functions that take a CvPlot parameter. (Eventually, const& should become the default for passing objects, but, so far, pointers are still predominant.)
    
    I had made a similar change for the CvMap::plot function last month:
    SHA 22e3de2096b84264109fddd7963632d2def71447

commit 58034739f147930b96823fd61539f36045a82169
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 27 15:05:34 2019 +0100

    Fix Ctrl+H (select hurt units)
    
    [change id advc.001z]
    
    When a city or fort tile contains units of different domains (land/ sea/ air), Ctrl+H selects all wounded units with the same domain as the currently selected unit(s). If no units of that domain are wounded, Ctrl+H has no effect.
    
    In Warlords (which introduced the shortcut), the domain was selected based on the internal order of the plot list and if no unit was hurt, all units became unselected and automatic unit cycling (if enabled) proceeded to the next group.
    
    Thanks to CFC user xyx for making me aware:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-19#post-15579814
    
    This commit includes some style changes in CvGame::doControl.

commit a26d4f836279ae955feb313770a510711b076bb5

    Repair the ChangePlayer component
    
    (I never really use that, but it's easy enough to maintain.)
    
    * Changing a player's civilization had been broken recently by change [advc.003u].
    * Changing a player's leader had reset the UWAI cache, which had resulted in failed assertions and faulty AI calculations for at least 1 turn.

commit d166644ae54c501cb441eebf322e201fb5020ddf
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Oct 22 02:38:25 2019 +0200

    Merge WtP changes to EnumMap; use EnumMap for CvPlot.
    
    Merged these five commits with some adaptations:
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@0e722861e223bf5a539a0f090b0af57a2f11c4ae
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@2ba6516fe1fc0c9483dc2175b0ed239b3b9b717e
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@36b40dac394f04a187c16f12498b76284494c405
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@60f3b062c59630668f0bebac0282ba1cb7da6466
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@baef68ffa57b39db61b21722ace5796ff90fbc6a
    
    Moved the helper functions for bitwise operations into a new header BitUtil.h
    
    CvPlot now uses EnumMaps.
    
    With just-in-time allocation and bounds checks handled by EnumMap, several CvPlot functions have become simple enough to define them inline in CvPlot.h. For the isRevealed/getRevealed functions that take a (so far mandatory) bDebug parameter, I've kept the implementation in CvPlot.cpp and added a new function with an inline definition and without the bDebug parameter. This way, the inline functions don't contain any branching. I've then removed bDebug=false from all call locations so that the inline functions are called from all non-UI code.
    
    Removed inline keywords from all EnumMap functions with conditionals in their bodies. When EnumMap was only used for CvArea, the inline keyword seemed to help a tiny bit, but, with CvPlot using EnumMap and many of the CvPlot getters inlined, aggressive inlining in EnumMap seems to hurt performance.
    
    CvArea no longer keeps track of the number of animals per player (not even for the Barbarian player). That statistic was unused.
    
    PROFILE_FUNC calls added to most of the write(FDataStreambase*) functions.

commit b7a3d7bb75e2fa7d9363dfcf9c14e3c3d9fb435e

    Merged parts of this commit:
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@a026f0e38c7379c2da6f9332a23333afd24df684
    
    Specifically, I've added the EnumMapInt class (unused for now) and

commit a22598147d3d3e46654435f574be670d7cdf5b9b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 13 21:21:24 2019 +0200

    FOR_EACH_ENUM macro added
    
    [change id: advc.enum]
    
    Rewrote CvEnums.h with macros that define global getEnumLength functions. For enum types that are fully known at compile time, getEnumLength returns the value of the last enumerator (e.g. NUM_DIRECTION_TYPES); the macros make sure that those enumerators are present. Exception: PlayerTypes and TeamTypes only have a getEnumLength function in an anonymous namespace (in EnumMap.h) because the macro shouldn't be used for players and teams.
    
    For enum types that represent info types loaded from XML, getEnumLength calls the respective CvGlobals::getNum...Infos function.
    
    This allows me to define a FOR_EACH_ENUM macro like the one proposed by Nightinggale here:
    https://github.com/We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod/issues/303#issuecomment-541334579
    
    So far, I'm using the macro only in a couple of places in CvArea.cpp. I might roll it out everywhere at a later time (perhaps along with the EnumMap).

commit c7394cfcb364a23e0ae9e93b52c9ccb32d10e071

commit ea0557d9c5871998292f1a741fe30e83c95e323c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Oct 10 01:17:06 2019 +0200

    EnumMap adapted to BtS
    
    [change id advc.enum]
    
    Removing enum types that exist in Colonization but not in BtS was trivial. I haven't added support for all BtS enum types that could be relevant; can add them as needed.
    
    I didn't want to merge two other "We the People" (WtP) optimizations at this time:
    1) New savegame format
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@4fe45c1bbad70f6d14df5a072f98cd4f5a0c14c3
    2) Global enums generated through an external (Perl) script
    We-the-People-civ4col-mod/Mod@576c95654034e7fe3d568bd5aabb1e6dba3e1112
    
    So I've replaced the Read and Write functions in Nightinggale's code with, I think, the simplest possible code for reading and writing the BtS format, and I've thrown out the JITArrayType data and set all the static byte-size information directly in EnumMap.h.
    
    As for 2), I've adopted the operator++ functions from WtP (CvEnums.h). The EnumMap classes call those functions. I've also added FIRST_... values to most of the enums (e.g. FIRST_PLAYER=0). Using an external code generator sure would've been nice for this – the preprocessor wasn't much help. The FIRST values aren't needed for the EnumMap, but I like the possibility to iterate over enum values without type casts.
    
    So far, EnumMaps are only used for CvArea. Everything else remains to be done.
    Enum variables as loop counters are only used in a few places in CvArea. Not yet sure if I want to expand that.

commit d5d48eef8fdfd54c7fb9d59d4dd08e3b01c6b346
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Sep 27 22:52:49 2019 +0200

    Remove non-human assertion from AI_getAttitude
    
    [change id advc.130u]
    
    I had added that in a recent commit along with parameters for ignoring the assertion. Seems to be more trouble than it's worth. I've now instead improved the computation of the attitude value assumed for human players by the AI: Friendly for teammates of the human player, Annoyed for human rivals of the human player and either Catious or Annoyed for AI rivals of the human player depending on the AI attitude toward the human player. Previously, it was Cautious in all those cases.
    
    This is probably better than most of the custom code that I use at some of the AI_getAttitude call locations, but it's difficult to track that code down (there are a lot of call locations), so I'll remove it as I happen to come across it.
    
    Attitudes within a team are now always treated as Friendly, even if the bForce parameter is set. That parameter only affects relationships of vassals and masters now.

commit 4527519ab57990ff79b80e6006748032cdaacea7
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Sep 27 09:12:31 2019 +0200

    AI denial conditions for city trades revised
    
    [change id advc.ctr]
    
    City trades remain work in progress. To be done (apart from testing and documentation): AI (counter-)proposals for city trades and, the main challenge, an overhaul and extension of the AI trade value computation. In this commit, I've added a parameter to CvPlayerAI::AI_cityTradeVal that allows the function to distinguish between the positive trade value of the recipient and the negative trade value of the current owner.
    
    Removed an obsolete financial trouble condition that had only applied to cities without any tile culture of the new owner – such trades aren't allowed by CvPlayer::canTradeItem anymore.
    
    Removed a condition that had prevented city trades within teams – the regular conditions should be OK for teams.
    
    Refuse ("take it from our cold dead hands") to cede cities with a high trade value unless at war. For now, use the trade value of the capital as a point of reference.
    
    Refuse to accept cities with a negative trade value. That can't currently occur, but, once AI_cityTradeVal has been revised, this condition should take care of financial trouble and worthless cities (currently handled by a separate AdvCiv function named CvCityAI::AI_isAwfulSite).
    
    Attitude-based conditions added: Never cede cities to the owner's worst enemy, don't liberate when Furious.
    For all other cases, there are two personality-based attitude thresholds per leader. One for cities where the current owner has barely any tile culture (less than CITY_TRADE_CULTURE_THRESH) and a (for some leaders) stricter threshold otherwise. I'll describe in the manual (still to be committed) how I chose the tresholds for each leader.
    For capitulated vassals, the true attitude is used – change [advc.130v] forces them to be Friendly toward their master. Added a new denial reason (not sure if it'll ever come up): "We don't truly like you that much."
    
    Don't give up any cities when close to a Domination victory and don't give up cities producing spaceship parts or high-production cities when close to a Space victory (unless liberation or at war).
    
    Refuse to accept cities under occupation when a third party has the highest city tile culture. (Computing city trade values during disorder is a problem yet to be addressed.)
    
    Two denial conditions related to vassals:
    * Capitulated vassals that are too small to break free refuse to trade cities to their master.
    * Masters refuse to trade cities to capitulated vassals that are almost big enough to break free.
    * Capitulated vassals refuse to trade cities to rivals ("it's out of our hands").
    Removed the BtS condition from canTradeItem that had prevented vassals from ever ceding cities.
    
    To prevent two human players from trading a city back and forth (for whatever purpose), CvPlayer::canTradeItem requires the new owner to have strictly higher culture if that civ has owned the city before and both trade players are human and not at war.
    
    Reverted a K-Mod change that had excluded cities that the AI will "never" trade ("take it from our cold dead hands") from the trade screen. The tile culture requirements for receiving cities in trade should already make sure that not too many uninteresting cities appear on the trade screen. When talking to non-rivals (vassal/ master/ teammate), the AI uses the more polite "surely you ask too much".
    
    Some time ago I had added a check for hostile units to CvCity::getLiberationPlayer; I've reverted that change, meaning that threatened cities can again be liberated – however, the AI won't accept them in trade if it can't defend them.
    
    (As a small UI tweak, I've hidden gold from a player's trade inventory when the other side has already put gold on the trade table. But it might be better to keep the amount of available gold on display, so I've reverted the change – but kept it as a comment because I'm still not sure.) [advc.004]
    
    Prevent the alerts added by AdvCiv from triggering when Alt+Z is used to cycle through the players. (The original BUG alerts still trigger though.) [advc.210]

commit 7bc68e5a42b54474b646a84cb64d5077bab8f9b6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Sep 25 12:52:57 2019 +0200

    Tweak/ refactor conditions for city trade and liberation
    
    [change id advc.ctr]
    
    Unless at war, a city can't be traded to a civ whose city tile culture is less than half of the current owner's. This is checked in addition to the 10% city tile culture requirement added a while ago.
    
    Allow liberation only when the prospective owner is a colonial vassal or has owned the city before. I think this K-Mod commit
    SHA d1f1ec44a4a99dde71f4e5cea574658fae682013
    had been responsible for liberation to arbitrary players (in some obscure circumstance) through the addition of the "base culture value". I haven't reverted that, only added an isEverOwned check.
    
    Check canTradeItem before showing liberate-upon-conquest popup. The popup says "return control to the ... empire" only if that empire has owned the city before; otherwise (i.e. when liberating to a colonial vassal), it says "let the ... empire take control." The "you liberated our cities" relations modifier is now always granted when liberating through the popup; it looks like this hadn't always been the case previously.
    
    (The liberation conditions are still too complicated; may have to simplify them at a later time.)
    
    Function CvTeam::canEnterPeacefully added that checks friendly (own, vassal or teammate) territory and Open Borders.
    
    Default value added for bConquest parameter of CvCity::getLiberationPlayer.

commit e1a152949829b846a839ade63ab1537f7735b691

    Mixed Continents: increase hill grain on small landmasses
    
    Same value as in "Continents and Islands" (C&I), but small ("snaky") continents also receive a higher grain value. commit f6e8caf701c5823dafc87cc4779fbba57d766091

    Don't obscure memory-based relations when memory>1
    
    Amendment to this commit:
    SHA 714de64ef00815f320a45f859c6f009fcb82a791
    
    Only concerns the random personalities option. commit 8c90b6fa7fafe4584b03d73d92a3808e8d1b2aa8
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Sep 19 22:35:37 2019 +0200

    Climate/ terrain adjustments (for all maps)
    
    [change id advc.129c]
    
    The +/-10 latitude region around the equator is no longer reserved for grassland (unless a map script explicitly sets a greater latitude interval – not sure if any do); plains can occur there just as well. This seems slightly more realistic (tropical soils aren't well suited for food production) and doesn't drastically alter the gameplay. Also makes maps more varied.
    
    The above change did not lead to more plains overall, but it did lead to fewer plains in the temperate zone. Since there was already a lack of anything resembling the Earth's steppe belts, I've increased the plains frequency a little bit and slightly decreased the grain value, meaning that plains tend to clump together a bit more.
    
    Deserts now have a tendency to appear next to plains. (Previously, there was a small correlation due to deserts not appearing near the equator where there was 100% grassland; but that's no longer the case.)
    
    Increased the frequency of hills a tiny bit.
    
    All these changes can be disabled by setting bEarthlike to False at the start of CvMapGeneratorUtil.py.
    (I've considered tying my changes to a new climate type, but it wouldn't have been flexible enough for what I wanted to do. Also, my changes are more subtle than those of the existing climate types.)

commit 0d49c21c210a7b5860ea1d2fd64020dfd605d208
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Sep 19 21:36:02 2019 +0200

    Overhaul of Continents&Islands (=Mixed Continents) script
    
    [change id advc.mxc]
    
    Grid size reduced a little [advc.165] and land/ sea ratio decreased (more water) so that the number of supported players and land/ sea ratio are approximately the same as on the standard maps (Fractal, Continents).
    
    Options "Add Water", "Add Plains" and "Reduce Desert" removed - but it should be fairly easy to re-enable them. They're not useless but pretty random (Why can't Desert be _added_? What about all the other terrain types?) and thus confusing. Better to adjust terrain frequencies through the Climate option or a new climate in Civ4ClimateInfos.xml. (In fairness, the plains frequency can't be adjusted through climate; can change it for all scripts in CvMapGeneratorUtil.py though.) I've, tentatively, kept the "Terrain Clumping" option.
    
    As for "Add Water", the script instead takes the sea level into account now. (All the Big/Small scripts ignore sea level.) Took a bit of experimentation, but I think the script is now producing the same land/ sea ratios as Fractal for all the sea level settings and independent from the overlap setting.
    
    World wrap option added – no reason why this script shouldn't have that commonplace option.
    
    Allow normal and massive continents also for the "Island Size" option. I don't think a "Small & Small" map (without continents) is going to play much better than Archipelago, but there's no harm in allowing it.
    
    Renamed some options to reflect that this isn't necessarily a Big/Small map. Made (normal) Continents and Snaky Continents the default landmass sizes for the two regions and made "Regions mixed together" the default overlap option.
    
    The number of tiny islands (added regardless of the landmass setting) is now based on the map size.
    
    Minor tweaks to the distribution of hills (hill grain).
    
    A bit of duplicate code (for filling the two land regions) folded into a loop.
    
    Use the default latitude thresholds for snow and tundra. (The BtS thresholds had been too low - or at least unrealistic -, but I've already addressed that through CvMapGeneratorUtil.py as part of change [advc.tsl].)

commit baa6c477e0c3be6a4a71e97a842108e84952c232
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Sep 17 15:18:16 2019 +0200

    Don't use human attitude value in AI code
    
    [change id advc.130u]
    
    Added an assertion to the AI attitude functions that warns when the attitude of a human player is accessed. Can pass bAssertNonHuman=false as a parameter to bypass the assertion.
    
    It's OK to use the human attitude for updating other AI values (e.g. strategy hash, worst enemy) that, ultimately, remain unused unless AI Auto Play is activated (or when a player retires from a multiplayer game). Actually, attitude and worst enemy get updated in those cases anyway, and the strategy hash could be (is already?) updated as well, but it's nice to have all the cached AI data available for inspection in Debug mode.
    
    An earlier change had already treated humans as being Cautious toward everyone, but I think it's better to address human players explicitly whenever the AI takes the attitude value of a rival into account.
    
    Fixed several uses of human attitude in the UWAI code, one in change [advc.109] and one in the K-Mod computation of espionage weights. [advc.120]
    
    Replaced some hardcoded thresholds for relations values in AI code with thresholds computed from the CvGlobals::RELATIONS_THRESH_... values loaded from XML.
    
    And a few unrelated changes to comments.

commit ef52c71628f14cf9751a2246ef520fce41617c28
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Sep 15 21:59:28 2019 +0200

    Improvements to AI city safety, stack strength evaluation.
    
    Prompted mainly by this post by Elkad:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-16#post-15540939
    
    [change id advc.139]
    
    When deciding whether to let a Great Person join a city or construct/ hurry a building there, the AI skips all cities that are seriously threatened by hostile units. There was some BtS code presumably with the same intention, but it only checked for hostile units inside the potential target city – where none can exist.
    
    The safety check at the start of the AI turn sequence now anticipates promotions and units in production that will appear at the end of the turn.
    
    After each attack by an AI unit, the unit owner checks if the attack has provided relief to any nearby threatened city – by repeating the safety check for that city. (This will matter very rarely.)
    
    The AI had probably been overestimating the effectiveness of larger stacks of low-strength units against smaller stacks of high-strength units – in the city safety check and in several other contexts. Two Swordsmen don't have a 50% chance of killing a Cuirassier. Hence [change id advc.159]:
    
    Added a function CvUnitAI::AI_currEffectiveStr that replaces most calls to CvUnit::currEffectiveStr. Moved duplicate K-Mod code for counting first strikes and collateral damage into the new function. AI_currEffectiveStr takes the per-unit strength values to the power of 1.25. This exponent is computed as 0.75 times the POWER_CORRECTION value set in AI_Variables_GlobalDefines.xml.
    
    This change could cause some problems with AI strength memory in earlier savegames because the (per-stack) AI strength values are on a somewhat different scale now. The memory gets updated at the end of each turn, so this shouldn't really be a concern.
    
    Unrelated minor changes:
    * Removed redundant function CvCity::getGeneralProductionTurnsLeft.
    * Fixed an "attitude cache out of date" assertion in Debug mode at game start. [advc.085]
    * Added back an include that is needed for the Profile build. [advc.make]
    * Improved my hack for hiding the promotion glow by renaming the exported function isPromotionReady to "isPromotionReadyExternal". Named the internal replacement "isPromotionReady". [advc.002e]

commit 714de64ef00815f320a45f859c6f009fcb82a791
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Sep 12 17:32:30 2019 +0200

    Bugfix: Relations display for random personalities
    
    Relations modifiers from remembered actions (e.g. "you declared war on us") had not been displayed when playing with randomized AI personalities. This bug must've been present ever since I merged the Show Hidden Attitude mod. Strange that no one ever reported it. Perhaps players thought it was intended to make the true leader personalities harder to decipher. E.g. only Gandhi applies a -2 relations penalty for declaring war on a friend. As a makeshift measure, I've hardcoded a list of memory types that can give away too much information. The game will display those modifiers as +1 or -1 even if the actual modifier is -2 or +2.
    
    And the game no longer shows the true total relations value after the attitude level. The sum of the displayed modifiers is shown instead (as had already been the case on the Glance tab of the Foreign Advisor screen). [advc.004q]

commit 1c56cc6ac149d97c3a28eae56440f4f0ab0183bd
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Sep 11 21:54:26 2019 +0200

    GET_PLAYER, GET_TEAM macros outside of AI headers
    
    GET_PLAYER is now defined in CvPlayer.h and CvPlayerAI.h (the latter definition takes precedence), and GET_TEAM and TEAMID are defined in CvGamePlay.h because I wanted to overload GET_TEAM to replace the TEAMREF(PlayerTypes) macro I had added early in development. Can't do that in CvTeam.h (not without messing up header inclusions).
    
    It would probably be better to use different getter macros for accessing AI objects (e.g. "PLAYERAI" instead of GET_PLAYER, "TEAMAI" instead of GET_TEAM), but I've decided that this isn't worth changing a three-digit number of macro call locations.
    
    CvGamePlay.h now only includes non-AI headers. For implementation files that need most of the AI headers, I've added a wrapper header CvAI.h. That header also re-defines the GET_TEAM macro (returning a CvTeamAI reference).
    
    This commit (more or less?) concludes my clean-up of the object-oriented design of the AI classes. One could now consider introducing sensible subclasses, e.g. for the Barbarian player/ team or something like CvAirUnitAI, CvSeaUnitAI ... I don't plan to do this in the near future though.

commit 3028ffa87b59a735f369fabe624741a377e02c0e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    Made the remaining virtual AI functions non-virtual
    
    [change id advc.003u]
    
    Made all the remaining "AI_" functions non-virtual (CvUnitAI and CvCityAI had already been cleaned up in earlier commits). Since some of them get called from the EXE as virtual functions, I've created virtual wrappers with private visibility (the EXE doesn't mind) that delegate external calls to the non-virtual AI functions. This improves safety and encourages the separation of AI and game rule code as AI functions can no longer be called on non-AI objects.

commit f25a2b91abefb15c4e5c4711ae21128a4660f48c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Sep 6 19:24:41 2019 +0200

    Relax single-landmass restrictions for resource placement
    
    [change id advc.129]
    
    The map generator no longer tries to place Fur, Gold, Silver and Gems on only one landmass.
    For some other resources (Spice, Wine, Incense, Dye), this restriction is also dubious, but the ones I've changed are clearly very unrealistic. As for encouraging trade, I don't think the landmass restrictions were crucial. Those resources are placed in clusters anyway.
    On that note, I've also decreased the probability of Gold getting placed in a cluster (for balance reasons).
    
    And I've added a limit for the number of resources of one type to be placed on a landmass: Can only place up to
    2 + ((number of tiles on the landmass) / 25).
    Excess resources are placed elsewhere; that can include small islands. (K-Mod had prevented single-landmass resources from getting placed on small islands - so islands resembling the Spice Islands had not been possible.)

    (I've wanted to implement this for some time, but only recently learned how to easily obtain option value descriptions from a map script.)

commit 1693567f87906859d16f815f72d7556d0a83f5af
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Sep 6 18:17:55 2019 +0200

    Perfect Mongoose: Avoid jungle, alpine tundra next to desert
    
    Avoid placing Jungle adjacent to Desert. (Grassland next to Desert is unfortunately still quite common.)
    
    Don't place Snow and Tundra on plots with low rainfall. Previously, Tundra and Snow representing alpine elevations were often placed next to Desert. Now, however, alpine Tundra/ Snow don't occur at all or very rarely. It seems that the script assumes very little rainfall (rain shadow?) in high elevations. That's an open issue.
    Set the latitude extremes back to +/-90 because, with +/-80, there was very little Tundra and Snow overall (due to the sea ice bands).
    
    Attempt to turn lakes fed by a river into bays only with a 50% probability.

commit 4cf124540a758a3d9ac76d043ad4238fd891a04e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Sep 2 17:47:13 2019 +0200

    Changed names of loop counters in some K-Mod code
    
    This old K-Mod commit
    https://github.com/f1rpo/AdvCiv/commit/c463b0d89baac8e4e4ae45afb44e3e97220a2f7f
    convinced me that loop counters really shouldn't be given names like "ePlayer" that are commonly used for other kinds of variables. The problem is that MSVC03 gives loop variables a scope beyond the body of the loop; see this CFC post of mine:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/cvgamecoredll-build-error-boost-python-list-hpp.648072/#post-15509430
    
    So I've changed all K-Mod loops where a variable "iPlayer", "ePlayer", "iTeam" or "eTeam" was declared in the loop header. Loops of the same pattern still exist – iterating over the various enum types –, but it's not worth the trouble to locate all those.

commit 22e3de2096b84264109fddd7963632d2def71447
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Aug 31 00:57:28 2019 +0200

    Replace plot/plotSoren calls with sth. slightly faster
    
    New function CvMap::getPlot(int x, int y) returning a CvPlot reference without performing any checks (apart from an assertion). [advc.003f]
    There were already two functions to map a pair of coordinates to a CvPlot object:
    
    CvMap::plot: Applies world-wrap. Shouldn't be used when it's clear that the given coordinates can't be off the map. So I've changed some calls to getPlot. Then removed the inline keyword because my test ran faster without it.
    
    CvMap::plotSoren: Returns NULL if either coordinate equals -1. Doesn't perform any other checks. Should be almost as fast as my getPlot function. The -1 checks are helpful when the coordinates come from a unit or city that might have been killed (but not deallocated yet). In most call locations, this can't be the case and then I've changed the call to getPlot – mainly because it's difficult to tell how "plotSoren" differs from "plot" (with getPlot, the return type CvPlot& makes clear that no safety checks are performed). But I haven't been able to remove plotSoren entirely.
    
    To make the CvPlot references returned by getPlot easier to use, I've changed some function signatures to accept CvPlot const& parameters. Some of these had been accepting CvPlot* (non-const) before, so I also ended up const-ifying some functions. [advc.003]
    
    Plus a small performance tweak for CvSelectionGroup::canMoveAllTerrain: CvUnitInfo keeps track of whether any unit type has the canMoveAllTerrain ability (no unit type does in BtS or AdvCiv). [advc.003b]
    
    My benchmark test has become about 5% faster as a result of this commit.
    
    And removed most of the _USRDLL preprocessor checks - there are plenty of exported inline functions now; hiding them from the EXE just in case that the source code might be released someday isn't reasonable.

commit 553b1a0f8d92b00f09f64f2ee1ecb4d696ebe43e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Aug 27 23:24:39 2019 +0200

    Moved DLL-to-Python calls and logging into separate classes
    
    New class CvPythonCaller. [advc.003y]
    To make (unused) Python callbacks less visible in the DLL code. Also improves error checking: by default, CvPythonCaller checks whether the Python function was successfully called. Found out about two (unused) missing Python functions this way; removed the one (doHeadquarters) on the DLL side, added the other (cannotSpreadReligion) on the Python side. This has required me to copy CvGameInterface.py from BtS.
    
    CvPythonCaller also handles the caching of the callback guards loaded from PythonCallbackDefines.xml. This is now done through an array of enum values. I've added some more callback guards, but the gains in performance are negligible (1% or so). The guards for Python events are now handled by the CvDllPythonEvents class.
    
    Moved the computation of game score and capture gold from Python to the DLL (CvPlayer). Not sure why these had been implemented in Python; perhaps as instructional examples for Python modders. I might want to change those formulas though, and that'll be easier (for me) in C++ (and faster).
    
    Similarly, I've moved the code that triggers the "Partisans" event from Python to the DLL (CvCity) and slightly changed it so that units spawn for the civ with the highest tile culture instead of the one with the highest city culture.
    
    New class CvDLLLogger. [advc.003t]
    To encapsulate the "message (control) log". That's used mainly for logging combat and random numbers (if "RandLog" is enabled in addition to "MessageLog").
    
    Changes made along the way – mostly style/ minor refactoring. [advc.003]
    * Disabled some more log output in CvEventManager.py by default. [advc.007]
    * The minimal distance between starting locations is now computed only once (by CvGame::updateStartingPlotRange) instead of computing it for every possible starting location in CvPlayerAI::AI_foundValue. [advc.003b]
    * Removed the empty public CvRandom::uninit function.
    * Removed some unhelpful Firaxis comments from init and reset functions.
    * Removed "public functions ..." and "protected functions ..." comments from most implementation files (not helpful in such large files).
    * Utility function "intToShort" added.
    * Utility function "narrowUnsafe" added for converting wide character strings to narrow character strings. Doesn't take into account locale and doesn't warn about characters that can't be narrowed – but at least these potential problems are now communicated by the function name. It's only used for map script names (so far).
    * Some refactoring in CvTeam::setHasTech and (related) in CvGame::doHolyCity and CvGame::doHeadquarters. Two bugfixes in unused code in doHeadquarters.
    * Refactoring in CvGame::testVictory.
    * Fixed a linker problem with psapi.h more properly (I hope). [advc.make]

    Split up CvInfos.h
    
    [change id advc.003x]
    
    To make the code for accessing XML data easier to work with, to reduce compilation time and to encourage encapsulation.
    For rationales for this particular way of partitioning CvInfos.h, see the comments in the new CvInfo_*.h files.

    * A few random style changes (not many). [advc.003]

commit 153270d44eafdb8916012598db069eec56fd8351
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Aug 22 00:31:31 2019 +0200

    Lazy loading of XML data for events and throne room
    
    change id [advc.003v]
    
    The XML files for random events aren't loaded until a game is started or loaded that has random events enabled.
    
    Similarly, the XML files for the throne room aren't loaded until the player accesses the Throne Room screen. (The Throne Room screen is an unfinished screen from Vanilla Civ 4 that can be accessed via the Debug menu - Ctrl+Shift+D in Debug mode.)
    
    Benefit: The first game start/ load after launching the game is now a (few?) hundred milliseconds faster. (If XML caching on disk was enabled and working, there would be close to 0 speedup.) Some memory saved, but probably negligible.

commit d844afa452d1c4a77b74bdcbfc802b89a014ab10
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Aug 18 01:18:21 2019 +0200

    Made most CvGlobals member functions const
    
    "GC" (global context) is now defined as a CvGlobals const& – was CvGlobals&. For calling non-const functions, CvGlobals::getInstance() needs to be used. That should serve as a warning, as most classes have no business changing global data. Not sure if const-ness can also improve performance in this case; certainly can't hurt.
    
    I haven't added const qualifiers to all CvGlobals functions that could have them, but most. Had to overload a lot of DllExports. The functions that provide references to singleton objects not owned by CvGlobals (in particular getGame, getInitCore and the getters for the various pathfinder instances) still return non-const references.
    
    The non-synchronized PRNG, which is owned by CvGlobals, is now accessed through a truly global function. Meaning that GC.getAsyncRand() calls throughout the code (not many really; mainly in CvPlayerAI.cpp) have been replaced with just getAsyncRand().
    
    The implementation files that set most of the data stored at CvGlobals – CvInfos.cpp and CvXMLLoadUtilitySet.cpp – simply redefine "GC" as a non-const reference, so nothing else has to be changed in those two files.
    
    Moved a little bit of code from CvMap to CvGlobals to remove a dependency of CvMap on CvLandscapeInfo. In preparation of splitting up CvInfos.h. [advc.003x]

commit 31edec670a86598be1ca207f00f5fcb0338b2b88
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Aug 17 00:55:13 2019 +0200

    Performance optimizations for access to XML data
    
    [change id mostly advc.003t]
    
    Added isAny... functions for some of the arrays in CvInfos.h. A recent commit had already deallocated empty arrays. The isAny... functions test if an array is allocated. Example (CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue):
    if (kBuilding.isAnyBuildingHappinessChanges())
      for (int i = 0; i < GC.getNumBuildingClassInfos(); i++)
        if (kBuilding.getBuildingHappinessChanges(i) != 0)
          iValue += kBuilding.getBuildingHappinessChanges(i) * ...
    This avoids looping through the 125 building classes when checking for the unused building-happiness-from-other-building ability.
    
    Integrated an empty-array check into the GC.getNUM...PREREQS functions; they take an enum value as an optional parameter now and check if the respective Info object has any prerequisites. Example:
    for(int i = 0; i < GC.getNUM_UNIT_AND_TECH_PREREQS(eUnit); i++)
      if(!kTeam.isHasTech((TechTypes)GC.getUnitInfo(eUnit).
          getPrereqAndTechs(i))
        return false;
    Won't enter the body of the loop if eUnit has no extra tech requirements. The gain in performance is probably tiny even across the code base, but at least one never has to think twice now before checking for prerequisites.
    
    Inlined all the CvGlobals::getNum...Infos and get...Info functions.
    
    Revised access to GlobalDefines. Integer GlobalDefines are now accessed in four different ways:
    * Access through CvGlobals::getDefineINT(char const*). This is still the default method for code that is clearly not going to affect the overall performance. In a few cases (e.g. in MapGenerator.cpp), I've at least moved getDefineINT calls out of loops and assigned their results to local consts instead.
    * Assign the result of CvGlobals::getDefineINT(char const*) to a local static variable. This is done when the value should only be used locally, i.e. when it's not really intended to be a "global" define. The new static variables are tagged with [advc.003b].
    * Enum value (enum GlobalDefines) in CvGlobals.h for fast access through CvGlobals::getDefineINT(GlobalDefines). For values used in multiple places or that may well be used in additional places in the future. The mapping between XML element strings and enum values is handled by a macro.
    * Access through a dedicated function without parameters; e.g. getEVENT_MESSAGE_TIME(). For pre-AdvCiv functions that can't be easily removed because of DllExport or because of a high number of call locations. Most of these (more than 50) I did remove.
    The USE_..._CALLBACK variables remain to be done.
    
    In most cases, the gain in performance is probably completely negligible. Even on the whole, my benchmark test has gotten only 3-4% faster, and that includes a few tweaks made before this commit. However, the goal is also to have to pay less attention to accesses to XML data in the future. Future (AI) code may also take more advantage of the isAny... functions.
    
    Added a parameter for default values and int-to-boolean conversion (getDefineBOOL) to the GlobalDefines getters in CvGlobals. This has rendered the getDefine... functions in CvBugOptions.h obsolete, so I commented those out.
    
    Misc. changes made along the way:
    * Can now set the AI attitude thresholds (e.g. +10 for Friendly) through GlobalDefines_advc.xml. [advc.148]
    * CvGame::syncRandPlot again allows random sampling if a positive iTimeout value is set. My previous code had ignored the timeout and always computed all eligible plots before selecting one at random. [advc.304]
    * When generating rivers, the standard map generator traverses the map in a random order. This might increase variety among generated maps a little. [advc.129]
    * Fixed a likely (minor) bug in CvUnitAI::AI_handleStranded. Units had been moving toward any coastal tiles including lakeshores. Now only seashores are targeted. [advc.001]
    * Fixed a potential problem with the UWAI function for measuring distances between coastal cities through coastal waters only (for pre-Astronomy naval wars).
    * If any of the BBAI victory strategies are disabled through XML, those settings are now ignored by the Rise & Fall game option. (Because R&F uses AI victory stages for scoring purposes.) [advc.700]
    * Shortened the display duration of announcements about founded religions and corporations. EVENT_MESSAGE_TIME_LONG is now entirely unused. [advc.106]
    * Refactored CvGame::setHolyCity and setHeadquarters. [advc.003]
    * Style changes [advc.003] and minor performance tweaks unrelated to XML data. [advc.003b]
    * Removed four remnant unused DllExports. [003i]

commit 437002d30474397556d9f633a925270144733674
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Aug 13 18:09:21 2019 +0200

    Break ties in resource placement order randomly
    
    [change id advc.129]
    
    During map generation, when the same placement priority is set for two types of resources in XML, decide randomly which type to place on the map first.
    
    Similarly, during starting plot normalization, go through the resource types in a random order when looking for a suitable food or extra resource.
    
    BtS relies on the order of the XML file (mostly alphabetic) in these cases. That reduces the variety of starting locations and causes Sugar (one of the last resources in the file) never to be placed on extremely crowded maps. With my changes, some resource type may still be omitted, but it won't always be the same type.
    
    These changes were prompted by this thread on CFC:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/always-missing-specific-resources-for-small-maps-islands-custom-continents.648468/

commit df136c50d7462e2185fc7874097a8a82f85cbc90
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Aug 13 01:04:01 2019 +0200

    Memory manager no longer sets newly allocated memory to 0
    
    Instead, memory is pre-initialized to 0xDADADADA as an error code in case that no proper initialization happens. Based on this Caveman2Cosmos revision by billw2015:
    https://sourceforge.net/p/caveman2cosmos/code/10955/#diff-5
    
    Note: AdvCiv only uses the memory manager for debug builds (through a K-Mod change).
    
    Change id [advc.make] - because I want to tie this change together with the earlier addition of the _NO_DEBUG_HEAP setting, which also prevents memory from getting pre-initialized to 0.

commit 0de04b1e4550ddf7c40e9fad939a722a907fc114
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Aug 5 13:42:29 2019 +0200

    FOR_EACH macros everywhere; changes to AI class design.
    
    FOR_EACH macros: FOR_EACH_DEAL and FOR_EACH_AREA added to cover the FreeListTrashArray (FLTA) members of CvGame and CvMap. Const/non-const versions for each macro. Had to add a hint file (cpp.hint) to get Visual Studio 2010 to parse the macro calls properly. [advc.003s]
    
    Replaced all the "iLoop" loops with macro calls. Applied some other tweaks to some of those loops. For the most part, these changes aren't tagged with any comments. If they are, change id [advc.003] is used.
    
    Added a lot of const qualifiers to function signatures, including some potentially problematic functions:
    * a couple of DllExports (overloaded as a workaround)
    * virtual functions (doesn't seem to hurt)
    * functions that may cache their results (CvCityAI.h; made the cache data in mutable)
    These qualifier additions were prompted by my use of pointers to const objects in FOR_EACH loops when possible. [advc.003]
    
    Revised most of the loops over CvDeal objects to use the new CvDeal interface added in a recent commit. I was able to remove most of the duplicate code this way (the same thing being done for the first deal player and second deal player). [advc.003]
    
    Changes toward salvaging Firaxis's object-oriented design of the AI classes: [advc.003u]
    * Added functions AI_getUnit and AI_getCity to CvGameCoreUtils; AI_getPlotCity and AI_getWorkingCity to CvPlot; AI_getGroup to CvUnitAI; and AI_getHeadUnit to CvSelectionGroupAI. The broader idea is to use handles to AI objects in return types and, outside of AI code, handles to non-AI objects in parameter lists and for local variables. Down-casts will still have to happen sometimes.
    * Added AI versions for the CITY, UNIT and GROUP macros. E.g. FOR_EACH_UNITAI declares the loop variable as a CvUnitAI const*.
    * Removed all but one pure virtual function from CvUnit. Apparently, the EXE doesn't call them.
    * Moved each group of the FOR_EACH macros into a separate header (e.g. FOR_EACH_UNIT to CvUnitList.h) along with an empty class derived from the respective FLTA class (e.g. CvUnitList extends FFreeListTrashArray<CvUnitAI>). These dummy classes hide the template parameter, meaning that CvPlayer.h no longer needs to include any AI headers. (But AI headers are still included in most of the large implementation files via CvGamePlay.h because I haven't yet dealt with the GET_PLAYER and GET_TEAM macros.) Also CvGame.h no longer needs to include CvDeal.h and CvMap.h no longer needs CvArea.h. Those headers are now directly included by those files that need them.
    * Revised the CvUnit and CvUnitAI (un-)initialization code so that the derived class calls functions of the base class (template method pattern) instead of vice versa (down-cast). Removed the reset and uninit functions because CvUnit objects (unlike e.g. CvPlayer objects) don't get reused.
    Similar changes remain to be done for CvCityAI and other AI classes.
    
    Lowered the AI trade value for embargoes a little bit. [advc.130f]

commit 715fa87579778a04e8da1adb5a6f1170f141aed5
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Jul 16 00:55:54 2019 +0200

    Several improvements to AI worker production and assignment
    
    [change id mostly advc.113]
    (A test on an Archipelago map with Tropical climate starting in the Modern era revealed numerous problems in the AI code.)
    
    Made the AI more reluctant to scrap excess workers. The scrap code hadn't yet been updated to the higher number of AI workers in AdvCiv.
    
    Clauses added to discourage the AI from training workers in colonies that had already been fully improved at an earlier time and need more workers only due to a new tech or new AI yield weights. It's often better to send workers via transport in such cases.
    
    Added code to avoid shipping out more workers than a landmass can spare. (The BtS/BBAI code was shipping out all idle workers.)
    
    Slightly increased the impact of forest and jungle on the number of workers needed at a city, and decreased the impact of the number of specialists.
    
    Lowered the maximal number of workers that a city may aim at from 5 to 4.
    
    AI_settlerSeaFerry renamed to AI_ferryWorkers. And fixed a likely bug: Only the workers needed by each potential target city had been counted, not the workers already available there. And some smaller tweaks.
    
    Cities on small island (3 or fewer tiles) can be left with 0 workers. (The AI is unlikely to found such cities but could also conquer them from a human player. An AI worker on a 1-tile island would look especially dumb.)
    
    Changes to the computation of workers available to a city: [advc.113b]
    * Renamed CvCityAI::AI_updateWorkersNeededHere to AI_updateWorkersHaveAndNeeded for clarity.
    * Made that function more efficient, addressing this BtS comment: "How slow is this? It could be almost NUM_CITY_PLOT times faster by iterating groups". A profiler run suggests that this change will reduce late-game turn times by 1 to 1.5%.
    * Idle workers that have retreated to the city tile are no longer missed when counting the available workers (bugfix, arguably).
    * Workers in cargo are not counted as available unless the transport is headed for the given city.
    * The number of workers available is updated over the course of a turn. (BtS does an update once per turn; updates throughout a turn happen in CvUnitAI::AI_improveLocalPlot and AI_nextCityToImprove, which covers only a fraction of the possible worker moves.)
    
    Made the AI less willing to speed up worker production through chopping. (If the AI has time to chop, then it can't be that short on workers.)
    
    Fixed the AdvCiv estimate of how busy the workers on a given landmass are; had only taken into account the number of needed workers, not the number of available workers. [advc.117,advc.121]
    
    Fixed bugs in AI_countNumImprovableBonuses (BBAI function). It had really only worked in the early game because Forts weren't handled correctly. [advc.001] (Not a major bug because the AI isn't and wasn't relying on that function much.)
    
    Performance tweak in CvUnitAI::AI_nextCityToImprove. Effect: Probably less than 1% speed-up; perhaps negligible. [advc.003b]
    And an even smaller tweak: Don't call AI_retreatToCity multiple times in AI_workerMove. [advc.003b]
    
    Made a minor tweak to the code that recognizes stranded units. [advc.046]
    
    Kludge added for a pathfinding problem in CvUnitAI::AI_pickupStranded. [advc.001]
    
    Refactoring in CvUnitAI::AI_load, CvUnitAI::AI_pickup and a little bit here and there. [advc.003]
    
    Removed all the "Returns true if a mission was pushed" comments from CvUnitAI.cpp.

commit ad0fd03d9476e947b828098800d566c605ec896b

    Walls and Castles are destroyed upon reconquest
    
    [change id advc.180]

    And refactored the loop in CvPlayer::acquireCity that decides which buildings get destroyed. [advc.003]

commit b96f30c2d50017ebf596b496c49a6e41b1b1cf7a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Jul 6 22:56:11 2019 +0200

    Several AI changes concerning workers
    
    (change id mainly advc.113)
    
    Made the AI willing to reassign a worker when a city has 2 assigned workers but requires only 1. This should make AI worker management quite a bit less inefficient.
    
    Removable Jungle is taken into account when computing the number of workers needed at a city.
    
    Reduced the upper bounds for the number of AI workers per city and overall.
    
    Made the AI more likely to train an additional settler before an additional worker when the current worker count is already close to the (national) upper bound.
    
    Made the AI less likely to train a worker in a city that needs 2 and already has 1. In particular, the AI will now rarely start the game by training 2 workers in a row.
    
    Made the AI reluctant to train several workers in parallel.
    
    Made the AI less likely overall to train nonurgent workers.
    
    Fixed a bug in AI code (CvCityAI::AI_getPlotMagicValue) that was unused in BtS and used by K-Mod mainly for deciding how fast to grow cities when happiness isn't a limiting factor. [advc.001] Now using that code also for deciding whether to grow cities before training a worker or settler.
    
    When deciding whether to grow before a settler or worker, the AI anticipates border expansion and improvements.
    
    And some other small adjustment to the AI evaluation of city growth. [advc.121,052]
    
    Increased the impact of resources (happiness, health, strategic) on AI found value a tiny bit further. [advc.131]
    
    Reduced UWAI "affection" cost a little bit further.
    
    Added a comment about the "blockage problem" assertions in CvUnitAI::AI_attackCityMove.
    
    A few insignificant non-functional changes in pathfinding code. (I was trying to track down a bug but eventually gave up. Seems rare and not too consequential.)
    
    Style changes in CvTeamAI::AI_calculateAreaAIType, CvPlayer::acquireCity (the FORCE_UNOWNED_CITY_TIMER code), CvCityAI::AI_updateWorkersNeededHere and a few tiny ones (spaces and parentheses) scattered in CvUnitAI.cpp and CvCityAI.cpp.
