commit 32d7dd438a3b00b05824be41ec01da28b1b4ffdd
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Jun 22 19:39:34 2019 +0200

    Exported functions with inline counterpart renamed via .def file
    
    change id: advc.003f (but manual still to be updated)
    
    Inspired by posts by alberts2 and Ang in the Caveman2Cosmos forum --
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/modders-documentation.441325/page-16#post-15476563
    -- I've added a module definition file that renames functions that the DLL has to export but shouldn't call internally: getX, getY, getOwner (in various classes), getGame, getMap and several CvMap functions. The new function names all have the suffix "External". The DLL should use the inlined versions instead.
    
    I've appended "INLINE" to numerous call locations - however, the next step (and the real point of this commit) is to remove the "INLINE" suffix everywhere to unclutter the code. This will be easy to do (automatic search and replace), but I want to wait a few days since this .def file thing is still new to me.
    
    I've already removed the "INLINE" from CvSelectionGroup::getOwnerINLINE and CvPlotGroup::getOwnerINLINE because the external versions of those functions weren't even called by the EXE.
    
    As for exported functions that miss a const qualifier, I've realized that a const function with the same name works just fine; no need to rename the original function through the .def file. So I've renamed my const function CvGame::gameTurn to CvGame::getGameTurn and used the same pattern for a few other (unimportant) functions. [advc.003]
    
    The .def file is enabled through Makefile.project. And I've also moved the /WX compiler flag to Makefile.project. [advc.make]
    
    (And, unrelated: commented out a bit of unused code in CvMapGenerator.py)

commit 09e2a07b068193d91136150fb85f040ead594cb1
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Jun 6 23:32:14 2019 +0200

    AI adjustments for military victory strategies
    
    The AI seemed to be much more successful with peaceful victory strategies. The following changes in the UWAI component are a step toward remedying that:
    
    Reduced fairness cost for dogpile wars, especially in the late game.
    
    Decreased the war utility counted for loathing and for kingmaking (the part that makes the AI try to thwart an enemy's victory).
    As these (pretty minor) changes had resulted in far fewer early wars, I've increased the utility counted for greed.
    
    Reverted an earlier change (from October) that had caused the AI to count war utility for coming close to a military victory already at stage 2 of a military victory strategy. I think this had mainly resulted in the AI being quicker to start wars, but, when a military victory is a long-term prospect, it's more important to build up military power. Instead of affecting war utility, the first two stages of the military victory strategies now have a greater impact on civics and research choices (replacing BBAI's AI_getWarThresholds function).
    
    When estimating likely winners, civs at stage 2 of a peaceful victory on a small landmass are treated as if their game score was 33% greater than it actually is.
    
    Some changes to AI_targetCityVal to make the AI target civs that aim for a peaceful victory earlier and more reliably. [advc.104d]
    
    Mostly unrelated:
    * Corrected a small oversight in the affection cost calculation.
    * Made the AI a bit less willing to raze Barbarian cities. [advc.116]

commit 4b02d149afbd6c68bb2664fe077d708d8084e36c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

commit 757230616770bddb7bf5caeebcfe1fe7ccc2b667
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun May 19 15:05:41 2019 +0200

    Amendment to land/water trade connection rules
    
    Restricted [advc.124] so that routes connect workable land tiles to water only on landmasses where the tile owner doesn't have any cities. (The intention is to let players connect workable tiles on islands without having to build a fort. Allowing long-distance coastal trade routes in the early game without a coastal city and connecting coastal resources with a single route segment were unintended side-effects.)
    
    Updated manual included.

commit 3e233e679412c94a509ff66c5f083c662a7db078
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    Last batch of style changes; some bugfixes and UI tweaks (large commit)
    
    Numerous minor refactoring changes in almost all modded C++ classes, especially in CvGame, CvGameTextMgr, CvPlot, CvPlayer(AI), CvTeam(AI) and CvUnit(AI). A big portion of the changes concern (jdog's) comment style and AdvCiv variable names. No further project-wide changes of this kind are planned.
    
    Changed all uses of INT_MAX and INT_MIN to the (presumably) equivalent MAX_INT and MIN_INT defined in CvGameCoreDLL.h – for consistency.
    
    long int vs. long long int error fixed in CvPlayerAI::AI_techValue (K-Mod code). Probably harmless. [advc.001]
    
    Sorted out duplicate code in BBAI's CvPlayer::initInGame and in the Change Player functions. [advc.003q]
    Also some in CvUnitAI::AI_pickup [advc.003]
    
    Worked around a problem with red lines under K-Mod's FASSERT_BOUND macro in the Visual Studio editor. Probably only an issue with VS2010. [advc.make]
    
    [advc.061] (help text for listing units in a tile) no longer uses the hardcoded mod name to determine the font size. Instead, the DLL now needs to be told what the font size is through GlobalDefines_advc.xml.
    
    Moved some settings that mod-mods may have to change to the start of GlobalDefines_advc.xml. [advc.009,002b,106i]
    
    AI bugfixes (AdvCiv code):
    * UWAI: AI civs at stage 3 of a peaceful victory had not been considering naval invasions to stop rivals at stage 4 of a peaceful victory.
    * Raze memory: The AI had considered all razed cities as insignificant, resulting in a reduced relations penalty. Moreover, 0 city culture now only implies 0 raze memory when auto-razing. [advc.130q]
    
    UI tweaks:
    
    Added a keyboard shortcut for unselecting all units: Shift + U [advc.088]
    
    Exiting the city screen through a right-click on the city tile now centers the camera on the city tile. All other methods of exiting jump to the selected units (if any) as before. [advc.004t]
    
    Tech help text on the tech tree now takes into account the current context (e.g. which wonders have already been completed) when hovering over any unknown tech. [advc.004]
    Previously, this change had only applied to techs that the active player was directly able to research.
    
    Debug mode: Contact text on the scoreboard shows culture info only when Alt+Ctrl is held or when a civ is close to a culture victory. [advc.007]

commit 20e0f168829b6befe2de4dc2f77f123c877c1bc0
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue May 7 02:12:39 2019 +0200

    Many style changes; header inclusions; embargo bugfix
    
    Style changes in CvCityAI, CvPlayerAI, CvDeal, CvDLLWidgetData and CvDLLButtonPopup, primarily in old AdvCiv code. Changed most of my variables names to Hungarian notation to match the BtS code. BBAI comments shrunk. AI_setMemoryCount function added. [advc.003]
    
    Header files: [advc.make]
    Sorted out the dependencies between the UWAI classes. To avoid having to include the UWAI, SPaH and R&F headers in CvGame.h, CvPlayerAI.h and CvTeamAI.h, I've turned the member objects into pointers. To make that work, I had to add a new header WarAndPeaceAgent.h for the inner classes WarAndPeaceAI::Team and WarAndPeaceAI::Civ; the bulk of the definitions in WarAndPeaceAI.h have been moved to that new header.
    Renaming the "WarAndPeace"/ "WPAI" stuff to "UWAI" remains to be done (perhaps).
    
    Added a wrapper CvGamePlay.h for CvGameAI.h, CvTeamAI.h and CvPlayerAI.h. All .cpp files that had previously included those three AI headers now include CvGamePlay.h. (As for the name "CvGamePlay", note that CvGame.h, CvTeam.h, CvPlayer.h are indirectly included as well. Those classes and the three AI classes are – unfortunately – tightly coupled.)
    
    AI_Defines.h no longer included in CvPlayerAI.h; instead included separately in the ca. 15 cpp files that need it.
    
    Bug fixed in [advc.130f]: stopTradingWithTeam had been called twice after negotiating an embargo. This had caused master civs to lose all deals with the embargo target when asking their vassals to stop trading (this isn't supposed to happen when a vassal stops trading) and had caused the AI to refuse to talk to a human instigator of an embargo for a longer time than intended.
    
    Bugs fixed in the [advc.099] formula for anger from foreign culture. Now works as described in the manual.
    
    Vassal tribute deals count half for "all the years you supplied us" (in BtS they count fully, previously in AdvCiv they didn't count at all). [advc.149]
    
    Reduced the AI probability of training a Worker. [advc.113] had increased that probability greatly; it remains higher than in BtS/K-Mod.
    
    Extended [advc.003n]: Assertions added to warn about uses of Barbarian AI memory.

    A few changes to avoid failed assertions, mostly for mod-mods.
    
    Suppressed an assertion in CvCity.cpp about overflow when a city's production is completed through a popOrder call from Python. That can happen in mod-mods or when the "+" cheat is used in Debug mode. [advc.064b]
    
    UWAI data for war planning is now updated right after a civ founds its first city. Not really relevant because the AI isn't going to plan any wars that early, but avoids triggering an assertion when AI civs meet while moving their starting Settlers. [advc.104]
    
    AI players added dynamically through Python (only relevant for mod-mods) are now hopefully handled correctly by UWAI. [advc.104r]

commit 3d7b629516be3367d6b21038d4f8b4b117573a01
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu May 2 11:58:44 2019 +0200

    Improved assertions in CvXMLLoadUtility
    
    Assertions added that warn when an XML tag expected by the DLL isn't found in XML – unless a default value is explicitly set in CvInfos.cpp. If the tag is defined in the schema, then the EXE should warn about it anyway, but the new assertions should help when a tag is also missing from the schema. And they warn about missing default values for non-mandatory tags -- although a default of 0, 'false' or an empty string as used by BtS is usually fine. I've added (explicit) default values where they are now necessary; didn't come across any actual errors in the current XML files.
    I had already added one such assertion in the past, but that was only for loading integers; now all data types are covered. [advc.006b]
    
    Unrelated, for multiplayer debugging: CvUnitAI::AI_patrol makes fewer entries in the MPLog. [advc.007]

commit e3a91c0d51cabdd82af2b11671710ac91e5173e6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Apr 15 23:51:30 2019 +0200

    Included headers revised
    
    Based on Nightinggale's guide at the end of this post
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/new-makefile-faster-compilation-profiling-and-more.499166/
    and the commit that the guide links to:
    https://github.com/Nightinggale/Medieval_Tech/commit/e4c77edc9667498ee0f97270c4db87afc4d5ea41#diff-66b042848b93af97de07513b9df496ae
    
    Change id: [advc.make]
    I've ended up changing include statements in more than half of the .h and .cpp files, and most of these changes aren't commented in the code.
    
    Removed about 20 includes from CvGameCoreDLL.h and instead added those includes only to those cpp files that need them. As proposed in the guide, I've moved the global inline functions for distance measurements from CvGameCoreUtils.h to CvMap.h. I went a bit farther by making them (non-static) member functions of CvMap.
    Relocated a few other inline functions from CvGameCoreUtils.h to get rid of included headers.
    
    To avoid including CvGame.h in CvInfos.h, I've rewritten the code that switches the Great Wall abilities on and off depending on the Barbarian options. The new code is also a bit nicer, though still mostly a hack. [advc.310]
    
    Removed all unnecessary includes that I could easily identify from cpp files. I've assumed that no further includes will be removed from CvGameCoreDLL.h, meaning that e.g. CvGlobals.h doesn't have to be included anywhere because it's already included through CvGameCoreDLL.h. Similarly, CvMap.h is assumed to cover CvPlot.h and CvArea.h.
    Reordered the include statements in most cpp files a bit so that related headers appear next to each other.
    
    Tbd.: Some 40 cpp files now include the trifecta of CvGameAI.h, CvPlayerAI.h and CvTeamAI.h. I want to see if I can't move the GET_PLAYER and GET_TEAM macros to CvPlayer.h and CvTeam.h. And perhaps include CvGame(AI).h in CvPlayer(AI).h, and CvPlayer(AI).h in CvTeam(AI).h to improve readability.

    Old build configuration merged into the new one

commit e81f6eab039ec78a56a030233e466ef698cf2241
Author: Erik Sandbraaten <erik.sandbraaten@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 3 12:13:59 2019 +0200

    BS2: Added a new configuration: "Final_Release"
    
    Enables additional optimizations by specifying /arch:SSE2 (utilizes "modern" efficient instructions), /GL (whole program optimizations) and the linker option /LTCG (link time code generation which enables more aggressive inlining and allows optimizations to span translation unit boundaries)

commit 4ff9ac45196d90fe3a9996df2cfe83e2c904a372
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Apr 9 19:36:44 2019 +0200

    Misc. bugfixes and tweaks; release candidate (v0.95rc)
    
    (DLL included)
    
    Amendments to previous commit:
    * Score difference cache is correctly serialized (I had goofed up the order of the read/write calls). [advc.130c]
    * No assertion about outdated attitude caches in Debug mode. [advc.sha]
    
    Increased AI production weight a bit again (I had recently lowered it). [advc.110]
    Decreased tech costs accordingly through the era modifiers. [advc.910]
    
    AI units no longer patrol in places that are more than 10 tiles away from any of their owner's cities. These patrols (in unowned land) had previously helped rival civs against Barbarians and were annoying to watch. [advc.102]
    
    Doubled the amount of gold per turn that the AI demands as tribute. [advc.104m]
    (An earlier version has added those demands; they happen quite rarely.)
    
    UWAI:
    Made the refuse-to-talk duration less unpredictable: Memory is increased by 2 upon declaring war and decays twice as fast as before. This only applies when war is declared on behalf of a third party. [advc.104i]
    The fairness mechanism to discourage early AI wars against human players now also covers games that start in the Classical era or later.
    
    Tribal villages are placed when starting in the Medieval era (previously only Ancient and Classical). [advc.314]
    
    Changed the BtS formula for applying bombardment damage so that counterintuitive rounding losses are avoided. E.g. bombarding a city with defense modifier 60% five times with a Catapult no longer results in a 21% defense modifier. [advc.004c]
    
    Bug fixed in [advc.033]: Naval blockades can no longer pass through non-friendly city tiles.
    
    Fixed a problem with a Barbarian Galley stuck in a loop when unable to reach any civ city. [advc.306]
    
    The Fractal map script may place land closer to the poles (by about 10° of latitude) and, on most maps (incl. Fractal), Tundra and Snow keep a greater distance from the equator than in BtS. [advc.tsl]
    In terms of latitude, Tundra had been appearing as far south as the Alps on Earth, and Fractal maps had strangely broad water bands at the poles (more so than e.g. Continents maps). This change should not affect the total land area nor the total area of any terrain type.
    
    The latitude value of tiles can be set from Python. I need this for a map script that I haven't committed yet, but it's also (marginally) faster this way as CvPlot no longer needs to compute latitudes on the fly. [advc.tsl]
    
    Minor tweak to my formula for the number of players assumed as standard based on the map size and sea level. [advc.137]
    
    The "Settings" tab of the Victory screen shows the start turn if it isn't turn 0. [advc.251]
    
    During AI Auto Play, the player's city billboards show the color of the player's civ instead of the population trend color (green/white/red). [advc.127]
    
    Turned the bitfields in CvPlot.h into regular booleans, which I expect to be a bit faster on today's hardware. [advc.003b]
    
    Refactored CvGame::testVictory [advc.003] after reading a question about it on CFC:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/quick-modding-questions-thread.351519/page-272#post-15421024
    And the Victory screen displays the target culture ratio for victory (if the iTotalCultureRatio tag is used – currently unused). [advc.004]
    
    Renamed some variables in CvGame::spawnBarbarians (AdvCiv code). [advc.306]

commit 7a48b42c2865dbda37bd00e61b9d37113789c3c8
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Mar 23 13:34:49 2019 +0100

    A few changes concerning AI civic requests and naval invasions
    
    Changed Suryavarman's favorite civic from Organized Religion to Caste System because asking others to change into Organized Religion (or Theocracy, Pacifism) generally doesn't make much sense unless the state religions happen to match. This was especially annoying in Sury's case because his change-civics requests apply a -2 relations penalty when rebuked. [advc.005a]
    (An earlier version of AdvCiv had already changed his favorite religion from Buddhism to Hinduism for historical accuracy.)
    
    When a player accepts an AI request to adopt a civic or religion and then switches out of that civic or religion, the relations bonus is forgotten faster (4 times faster to be exact). Likewise, the relations penalty from refusing to switch is forgotten faster (3.5 times) when the player makes the requested switch later on. Previously, AdvCiv had suspended the relations modifier in such situations, but I've come to think that this makes it too unattractive to accept AI requests. [advc.145]
    
    Disabled [advc.162] (units that enter enemy borders on the turn that war was declared lose all remaining movement points). I don't think it's quite worth the added complexity all things considered, but the change works alright and can be re-enabled through GlobalDefines_advc.xml.
    
    When an AI stack is about to declare war, it tries to avoid moves through the enemy's territory that would lead to a declaration of war earlier than necessary. There was already BBAI/K-Mod code for this, but that only stopped the AI from ending a move in the enemy's territory; passing through in a single move wasn't covered. [advc.082]
    
    Another small tweak to [advc.048] to prevent the "Press ALT for best odds" hint from being shown unnecessarily when units are tied for best odds.
    
    A few more tech cost changes. [advc.910,advc.251]
    
    When a game ends, the "Demographics" tab shows information as if the player knew the demographics of all rivals. [advc.077]
    (This wasn't an issue in BtS because the "Demographics" tab never hid any information.)
    
    For autosaves in multiplayer, it is now assumed that the game name "chipotle" implies that this is a test game run on a single machine. Only players with even id numbers create autosaves then (to avoid error popups from writing to the same file at the same time). [advc.135c]

commit ebbd389356b94a0e5269c0fce27954366a8828e7
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Mar 20 01:25:56 2019 +0100

    2 bugfixes (UWAI, K-Mod) and some misc. tweaks
    
    Sign error fixed in UWAI; must've been in the code since the first AdvCiv release. This had caused the AI to treat anticipated losses of its vassals as a good thing.
    
    Made about 20 of the AI leaders more reluctant to offer peace. If an AI-initiated peace offer is rejected (and UWAI is enabled), the AI will offer slightly worse peace terms when contacted for peace until the contact timer is back at 0, i.e. for 8 to 20 turns. [advc.134a]
    
    AI evaluation of commerce modifiers improved; the AI should value the Education tech more highly now. [advc.131]
    
    Bugfix: K-Mod's "Simple Unit Selection" option had had no effect because the option id set in XML differed from the one checked by the DLL. [advc.001]
    Enabled that option by default. [advc.004]
    
    A small addition to the last commit: When the Alt key is used to pick the attacker with the best odds, the sacrifice value is used as a tiebreaker so that less valuable units are preferred. [advc.048]
    (And the last commit was missing the declaration of CvGame::setAIHandicap.)
    
    Revolt alert shows revolt probability only at permille precision (not per 10000). [advc.210b]
    
    When a city under occupation is traded, units aren't bumped out of tiles surrounding the city. [advc.122] (BtS lets the new owner momentarily take ownership, bumps units out, sets the occupation timer and takes tile ownership away again because cities under occupation don't have a culture range.)
    And the AI attitude cache is updated after liberation so that the change in relations takes effect right away.
    
    Trade routes are updated when anarchy starts or ends. (Because AdvCiv doesn't allow trade routes with civs in anarchy.) [advc.124]
    
    Fixed(?) an issue with the [advc.004c] formula for city bombardment. Previously, the decrease of the city defense value was sometimes off by 1.
    
    The "reduced city defenses" message shows the defense percentage without Walls and Castle if the bombarding unit ignores building defense. [advc.004g]
    
    Help text for units in a tile [advc.061]: improved the estimate of the available space to avoid going off screen when units in a large stack have many promotions.
    
    Refactoring in CvCity::setHasReligion, CvCity::updateTradeRoutes, CvUnit::bombard, CvPlayer::setCivics, CvPlayer::changeCapitalYieldRateModifier, and a little in CvCityAI::AI_buildingValue and CvGame::selectUnit.

commit 9db17a1fc6c34841711187b3f2c17961951dd1ca
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Mar 19 17:26:05 2019 +0100

    Alt key for finding attacker with best odds; and a few tweaks.
    
    When a human player attacks or views combat odds with multiple units selected, the unit with the highest survival odds is chosen as the attacker if the Alt key is held down. If Alt is not held, the AI may select an attacker with suboptimal odds, e.g. to inflict collateral damage or to preserve high-level units. [advc.048]
    (In BtS, the attacker with the best odds was -usually- displayed, but, when the attack was ordered, the AI was free to choose a different unit.)
    Refactored CvSelectionGroup::groupAttack and CvSelectionGroupAI::AI_getBestGroupAttacker a bit in the process.
    
    The change in unit expenses predicted by [advc.004b] now takes into account units in cargo when hovering over the Delete button of a transport unit.
    
    Research overflow is shown as part of the solid portion of the research bar only if tick marks are disabled. With tick marks, it's shown as part of the semi-transparent portion. [advc.078]
    The way BtS displays overflow (always solid) suggests that the overflow has already been spent, but it isn't spent until the end of turn. That's also inconsistent with the production bar.
    
    Revolt probability is displayed as 0.1% (instead of 0.0%) even if the actual probability is a bit smaller than 1 permille. [advc.101]
    
    Tweaked a recent change [advc.144] so that the AI may
    * ask for a gift despite a peace treaty if 3 or fewer turns of peace remain, and
    * demand tribute if 1 turn of peace remains.

commit 80cd96df1b7dae26c0fbb2d85a422f97610b09fe
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Mar 13 22:32:54 2019 +0100

    Changes to overflow and hurry AI
    
    Overflow rule changes: [advc.064b]
    * Removed the K-Mod code that assigns excess overflow from a trained unit to an additional unit of the same type. Rationale: See release notes (to be published) or manual.
    * Chopping production is no longer converted into overflow and instead stored separately until needed. Chopping can thus never lead to overflow gold.
    * The current overflow and chopping production are subtracted from the production that Slavery needs to add. Consequently, Slavery can't be used at all when the entire production cost is already covered by overflow/ chopping.
    * The same goes for rush buying, except that all city production (including tile yields) is subtracted.
    * When a production order will finish at the end of a turn, the production yield tooltip on the city screen shows how much production will carry over to the next order from overflow and chopping and how much overflow will be converted into gold.
    * The game shows a message when overflow is converted into gold.
    * Some minor changes to [advc.123f] (fail gold only for queued wonders) to integrate that change with the overflow changes.
    
    Changes to hurry production (rules, UI): [advc.064]
    * Can't sacrifice more than 3 citizens at once for Slavery. [advc.064c]
    (I meant to make some changes to simplify the wonder hurry modifiers, but this got too difficult to implement, so the above is the only change aimed at wonders.)
    * The two BUG Whip Assist options for including the current production rate in the overflow calculations are now enabled by default, and, even if disabled, the current overflow and chopping production are taken into account.
    * The hurry Civ4lerts use the DLL overflow computation; outdated Python code commented out.
    * Option added to the "City Screen" tab of the BUG menu for disabling or enabling the hurry tick marks independently from the progress tick marks. Hurry tick marks disabled by default.
    
    AI changes for Slavery: [advc.121b]
    It turned out that my earlier attempts to make the (K-Mod) AI use Slavery less hadn't accomplished much, and that the (lack of) urgency of a production order hardly mattered – but it should matter because if an AI city produces frivolous things, then converting food into production isn't desirable. With my new changes, the AI still uses Slavery a lot, but only on good stuff like Settlers, Workers, essential buildings and military units with an immediate use, or to get rid of unproductive population.
    
    AI yield priorities shifted a bit from production to commerce. [advc.110]
    
    AI tech rates have become faster, so I've increased tech costs through the per-era modifiers by some 5-10% overall. [advc.910]
    (Tbd.: May have to reduce the AI bonuses from difficulty instead if the higher tech costs change the pace of the game too much for humans.)
    
    Reduced the size of the "city hunting stack" that BBAI trains when there is no war plan. [advc.017]
    
    Added code that causes the AI to train a few ships for land wars (transportation, bombardment), though only under fairly narrow conditions (in particular, the city that the AI targets has to be coastal), and code for training extra ships when there are enemy ships in AI territory. [advc.081]
    
    Fixed/worked around an issue with [advc.040] (or perhaps really a bug in non-AdvCiv code) that had caused ships with a loaded Worker (other units too?) never to disembark. It seems that transports can remain targeted by CvSelectionGroupAI::AI_getMissionAIUnit when the group has already been loaded.
    Also, the AI now builds a ship for transporting Workers eventually, even when there is no other reason for having a transport ship.
    Extended [advc.040] so that the AI will improve not just island tiles workable by a mainland city, but also mainland tiles workable by an island city.
    
    Loading-screen hint added about the replay format. [advc.106i]
    
    Random refactoring: waterArea functions (CvPlot), CvUnitAI::AI_greatPersonMove, CvCity::hurry and a few little things in CvPlayerAI::AI_chooseProduction. [advc.003]

commit 73451648e722a7f35a85195d7b683c2028f162f5
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Mar 8 14:13:08 2019 +0100

    Change overflow handling (work in progress)
    
    [advc.064b]
    On-screen message added that tells the player when a city has used excess overflow to train additional units.
    
    Set the upper bound for the overflow that a city can store to the maximum of the city's food store size and (as before) its base production rate. The cost of the last completed production order no longer matters. This should fix balance problems with AI cities training multiple Archers per turn through Slavery on the highest difficulty levels.
    
    However, I'm going to disable and remove the K-Mod mechanism for training multiple units per turn, so this commit is only an interim result.

commit 65a1472094e89d913ccf565c76687027a530a30d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Mar 6 22:39:00 2019 +0100

    Changes to AI greetings
    
    Only about half of the AI leaders (based on CONTACT_DEMAND_TRIBUTE) brag about their best units. When a braggart AI has a new best unit, it brags about that unit at the first opportunity (unless the best unit is known anyway because AI technologies and resources are visible to the human player) and, if contacted again, with a random chance as in BtS. This eliminates the need for contacting the AI multiple times to find out its best unit in the early game. [advc.079]
    
    Partially revised the CONTACT_DEMAND_TRIBUTE divisors in the LeaderHead XML file. For example, Shaka, Ragnar, Mehmed were among the least likely AI leaders to demand tribute (divisor 1000); now they're among the most likely (divisor 25), whereas e.g. De Gaulle and Isabella are no longer very likely to make demands. I've done this to support the change to bragging (want the early warmongers to brag), but also to match the historical background better. [advc.005a]
    
    The AI remembers when it has warned a human player against trading with a particular enemy, and is more likely to warn if it hasn't warned before and less likely otherwise. Mainly to reduce the frequency of the accompanying leader animations, which are somewhat jarring.
    After the first era, the AI says "we would encourage you to stop trading ..." in the greeting only if the human player has annual deals with the worst enemy. [advc.079]
    
    And some unrelated changes:
    
    Warning about XP loss added to unit upgrade button. [advc.080]
    Related CFC thread: https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/k-mod-far-beyond-the-sword.407049/page-149#post-15396176
    
    Fixed an issue with [advc.004h] (city radius colored around selected Settler): The color had lingered after deleting a Settler, and occasionally, after founding a city.
    
    In scenarios, the start era is set to the mean of the player eras. This blocks some problematic Ancient wonders in the Earth1000AD scenario. See this CFC post: https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/earth-1000ad-shadow-game-sunset-invasion-invading-europe-with-aztec.643333/#post-15396111

commit 517b49c46ac476afd0dcc59d9f61861eaf672dd1
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Mar 5 19:29:08 2019 +0100

    Demographics tab revised; option to hide GP bars at game start
    
    Changes to the Demographics tab, mostly to allow fewer conclusions to be drawn in the early game: [advc.077]
    - The best and worst columns show the value, name and rank of the best or worst rival whose demographics are visible through espionage.
    - The rival average is rounded to the nearest multiple of 5, no longer includes vassals and teammates of the active player (those aren't rivals) and isn't shown when there are fewer than 4 rivals alive. (Because, with just 3 rivals, if best and worst are known, the one in the middle could be computed from the average.)
    - Full info is shown in Debug mode.
    - Layout revised to accommodate ranks and names in the best and worst columns.
    - Cosmetic changes to all headings in all languages.
    - Removed the final row (Export/Import) because there wasn't enough space anymore.
    
    Options toward the top of CvInfoScreen.py:
    - Show the final row (will result in a vertical scrollbar). Before disabling it, I had changed it so that only exports are shown (i.e. total commerce from foreign trade routes).
    - Show a "?" in the best and worst column when the demographics of the best or worst rival aren't visible. (Instead of showing the best or worst one whose demographics are visible.) Or (third option): Show the name of the best or worst rival even if its demographics aren't visible; "?" for rivals that haven't been met.
    
    A note on the implementation: Pretty bad, though arguably no worse than before. This really needs a class 'Demographic' to manage, among other things, the row numbers.
    
    This post (by Long try) demonstrates some of the problems with the BtS screen:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/the-sigh-emperor-warm-up-exercise.643113/page-2#post-15392740
    
    Option added to the BUG menu ("General" tab) for showing the GP bars only once there has been any progress toward a GP. Disabled by default (and the bars also remain disabled by default). [advc.078]
    
    SPaH option: "Dawn of Man" (DoM) screen is shown after regenerating the map. [advc.004j]
    
    Fixed an inconsequential bug in the PerfectMongoose script. [advc.021b]

    Wake up cargo when a ship reaches land

    Bugfixes (in AdvCiv code); enhanced current deals on the Trade screen

    Fixed a minor bug (also introduced in some recent commit) that had triggered a spurious willing-to-talk alert after hiring an AI civ for war. [advc.104i]
    
    Fixed a minor (potential) issue with [advc.046] (unloading of units in order to pick up stranded units).
    
    Found a way to obtain the CvDeal object that corresponds to the trade item that the EXE provides when calling CvDLLWidgetData::parseTradeItem and CvPlayer::getItemTradeString. This allowed me to make the following improvements to the list of current trades on the Trade screen: [advc.072]
    * Hover text for trade items shows the deal that the item belongs to (e.g. "Banana to Peter for Rice and 2 gold per turn" when hovering over "Banana") and whether/ when that deal can be canceled.
    * No trade denial is shown when hovering over resources that are being traded.
    * The "Deal Turns Left" option on the "Advisors" tab of the BUG menu now has four choices: Show the number of remaining turns
    - only on the "Active" tab of the Foreign Advisor screen,
    - only in help text (still the default), and new:
    - only in the list of current trades on the Trade screen, or
    - both on the "Active" tab and the Trade screen.
    The new choices will e.g. show "Open Borders (8 Turns)" in both columns of the Trade screen when Open Borders have been signed two turns ago.
    
    Double-clicking the city tile no longer exits the city screen. (Because this shortcut collides with the one for enabling citizen automation - a single click on the city tile.) [advc.004t]

    Loading-screen hint added about assigning a working city to tiles that multiple cities can work. [advc.008d]
    
    When an AI civ checks if there are any good resources near a potential city site, resources in tiles that the civ already owns are counted so long as they aren't within the radius of any existing city. Such resources had previously been disregarded (which had prevented the AI from settling Crete in my EuroWorld scenario). [advc.031]
    
    Refactoring in CvPlayerAI::AI_updateFoundValues and a little bit in CvPlayerAI::AI_foundValue and CvPlayer::setTurnActive. [advc.003]

commit b3272cda385d064bcc030dd9756913da4a42d422
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jan 30 20:39:04 2019 +0100

    Addressed some minor issues and got side-tracked into some additions
    
    More work on PerfectMongoose to improve the distribution of the starting locations. [advc.021b]
    * The distances between potential starting locations on different landmasses are now taken into account (in addition to the more important distances between locations sharing a landmass).
    * Tweaked the algorithm for eliminating potential starting locations that aren't local optima.
    * Bug fixed (introduced by me) that had usually prevented the "Old World Starts" option from reserving a large continent for the New World.
    * Meteors can no longer strike water tiles. (The goal of the meteors is to turn coastal water into ocean. I think striking the surrounding land has a better chance of accomplishing that.)
    * Added some log output (PythonDbg.log).
    Some starting locations still tend to be too close together. I think the main issue that remains is that landmasses are processed individually, without taking into account other landmasses reachable across coastal water. Some of the landmasses that are currently ruled out on account of being too small are part of island chains that could actually support a player.
    
    Workable tiles with a route have a trade connection to adjacent water tiles. This means, a resource on an island within the workable radius of a (mainland) city doesn't require a Fort in order to be connected. [advc.124]
    See this CFC thread for an example:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/how-do-i-connect-up-this-resource.639015/
    
    Fixed an issue with [advc.121]: Code for making the AI prefer Forts over cheaper improvements on resource tiles where a Fort can act as a canal had had no effect.
    
    Bug (crash) fixed that I had introduced in a recent commit. [advc.rom4]
    
    Global Warming no longer turns Forests into Jungles; removes the Forest instead. [advc.055]
    
    When multiple members of a team are researching the same tech, their research modifiers are decreased by 10 percentage points. [advc.156]
    (This is supposed to make tech decisions more interesting.)
    
    In multiplayer, when a tech is discovered by a teammate, the "you have discovered" sound is played. The tech quote is only played for techs researched directly by the active player. Was already supposed to work this way in previous versions; now hopefully correct. [advc.156] (previously under id 201)
    
    Help text for tech (e.g. when hovering over the research bar) shows all research modifiers that apply, i.e. the penalty from team research mentioned above, but also bonuses from diffusion and from knowing multiple prereq techs. [advc.910]
    
    Option added to the "Map" tab of the BUG menu for showing trade network icons above the city bars; disabled by default. [advc.002f]
    (Previously, the icons were disabled without an option.)
    
    Optional airport icons merged from BULL; enabled by default. [advc.002f]
    Had to add BULL's GameFont.tga for this, which will increase the release download size by about 170 KB.
    
    Messages about "vigilant" rival spies are shown in white, not in red. [advc.120]
    
    Less vertical space wasted on the "Info" tab of the Foreign Advisor screen. Same treatment as for the "Active" tab in a recent commit. [advc.066]
    This is only relevant if the BUG Info tab is disabled (which is the case by default).
    
    When two civs meet during the placement of free starting units, only a diplo popup is shown (no on-screen message) because the BUG mod isn't yet initialized at that point, so the player's preference can't be taken into account. [advc.071]
    
    Worked around a strange issue with the choose-production popup appearing twice after founding the first city in networked multiplayer games. [advc.124g]
    
    Refactoring in CvPlayerAI::AI_foundValue (minor) and in CvUnitAI: AI_improveBonus and AI_pickTargetCity. [advc.003]

commit 54cbd1453cba15b0f876a847e506fe1663b293c2
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Jan 22 20:24:17 2019 +0100

    UWAI affection cost tweaked
    
    UWAI: Made the AI less willing to go to war against a liked civ:
    * Previously, attitude had been ignored once war preparations were concluded. Now, if war remains imminent for more than 3 turns, 10% of the affection value computed from attitude is subtracted from war utility, and another 10% for every further turn. Rationale: Don't want to allow human players to pacify the AI through e.g. a gift once AI units approach the border, but the AI mustn't ignore (changes in) attitude for too long.
    * Increased the base weight of the affection value from 90% to 100%, but the weight now decreases toward 80% over the course of the game, meaning that the AI becomes slightly more callous over time.

commit 66c00fd402cfadd3845f449300eb56850fdff077
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Jan 22 00:18:05 2019 +0100

    Issues with AI plot danger functions fixed
    
    A more proper fix for the BtS bug that causes the AI plot danger functions to ignore hostile units that have attacked on their last turn. The previous fix had sometimes overestimated the danger, which was OK for the AI, but the function is, as I've now learned, also used for human civs, e.g. to interrupt Workers when they are threatened. [advc.001k]
    
    And, as an extension of [advc.128] (makes AI visibility cheats less obvious), the plot danger functions don't cheat with visibility when used for a human civ, and only sometimes (probabilistic based on a hash value) cheat with visibility when used for an AI civ.
    
    And some refactoring in the plot danger functions. [advc.003]
    
    Inlined some very frequently called CvPlayer and CvTeam functions. [advc.003f]
    
    Removed the PROFILE_FUNC macro from some functions that have a negligible total computing time despite being called very often. And from the extremely frequently called CvUnitAI::AI_plotValid. I hope this will make the profiler run a bit faster. [advc.003o]
    
    (Unrelated) bug fixed in [advc.070]: The text color for a negative gold rate had not been applied.

commit bf48af8b3529f23c93ddbf21fde05e6b4ad8539a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Jan 21 01:13:38 2019 +0100

    Many misc. tweaks
    
    A heads-up to anyone following this mod on GitHub: I will perhaps migrate to GitLab after v0.95 (as GitHub doesn't support any of my web browsers anymore). Project URL on GitLab:
    https://gitlab.com/f1rpo/advc/commits/master
    For the time being, I intend to push to both GitHub and GitLab.
    
    Testing for an experimental release begun.
    
    --
    DIFFICULTY SETTINGS
    
    Production modifiers from difficulty only apply half to Settler units. (Prior to a recent commit, they hadn't applied to Settlers at all.) I've noticed that all growth modifiers (including the AI modifiers in BtS and the human modifiers I've added) also apply to the cost of Settlers. As a result, Settlers had been too expensive on the high difficulty settings, e.g. 150 production on Deity (compared with e.g. Worker: 80). Now Settlers cost 125 production on Deity.
    
    Human worker build times increased on the highest three difficulty levels. AI work rate bonuses reduced. (Rationale: Worker speed should match research speed, otherwise it's too difficult to keep the first Worker occupied. As even a small work rate penalty would increase the build time of every build including Road, I'm using a build time modifier instead.) [advc.251]
    
    No second free AI Settler on Deity; had been so quick to expand that the player usually didn't stand a chance to found more than three cities on a Standard map with the default civ count. I'm not sure if Deity can be beaten now on normal settings (I don't think I can), but at least the player doesn't get totally boxed in. [advc.250e,advc.251]
    
    Clause added to discourage the AI from trying to steal tiles in the radius of a rival capital whose borders haven't expanded yet. (Since I've removed the free Settler on Deity, this only - possibly - matters when starting in a later era.) [advc.031]
    
    Tweaked the production and research modifiers on the lowest difficulty levels; I think production was too slow compared with research. [advc.251]
    
    Increased the tiles per animal on Prince difficulty and higher by 5, and tiles per Barbarian land unit on Monarch and higher also by 5. On the highest settings, Barbarians were too dangerous considering the production cost increases from [advc.251]. Increased the start turn number for the placement of Barbarian units and cities by 5 for all difficulty levels. [advc.300]
    
    --
    UNIT AI
    
    Changes to naval blockades: [advc.033]
    * Ships (except Privateers) can no longer blockade inside the Open Borders of another civ.
    * Non-Privateers can't blockade at all when at peace with everyone, and blockading units are awoken if a blockade is no longer allowed. Taken together, these two changes should help against forgotten ships that continue to blockade after a war.
    * CvTeam::isMinorCiv and CvTeam::getAtWarCount are cached for better performance. This might matter for the bullet above because getAtWarCount is now called by CvTeam::canPlunder, and canPlunder is called for every tile in the blockade range. Savegame compatibility is maintained (but this was a little tricky to do). [advc.003m]
    * Added a function CvUnit::blockadeRange for code shared by updatePlunder, collectBlockadeGold and CvGame::updateColoredPlots. This should also address some minor inconsistencies between them. Also using a faster pathfinder function now (one with a range limit), and avoiding some plot group updates. These changes reduce the delay when starting/ending a blockade with a non-Privateer unit (but don't help much with Privateers).
    
    Fixed an issue with [advc.163] (units lose all moves when teleported): Can now handle AI units getting bumped out of foreign territory while attempting a sneak attack. The underlying issue isn't fixed though: When a border tile flips as the AI is about to declare war, the AI doesn't return to friendly/neutral territory before declaring war.
    
    Re-enabled an assertion that warns about AI units unable to select an order (I had, unwisely, disabled that in v0.8 I think). Found and fixed the following bugs:
    * AI sea workers had been trying to build routes. [advc.001y]
    * Change [advc.049] (no AI routes through human territory) mustn't pass the SAFE_TERRITORY flag to the pathfinder.
    * Fixed an issue with [advc.004k] (Sea Patrol mission removed): The AI had been unable to guard its coast, and had been calling CvUnitAI::AI_update 100 times before letting its idle ships skip their turn instead.
    
    --
    WAR AND PEACE
    
    Fixed an issue with UWAI's fair-play mechanism: When the AI expanded much faster than the human in the early game (Deity, perhaps also Immortal), the AI had been writing the human off as doomed and had attacked without regard for fair play.
    
    AI willingness to be hired for war: UWAI now checks if gold trading is available before assuming that a human player could procure some extra gold to sponsor a war.
    
    UWAI now respects the contact delay for capitulation offers, and doesn't try to sue for peace if the BtS AI would still refuse to talk. [advc.104i]
    And tidied up CvPlayerAI::AI_isWillingToTalk.
    
    Fixed: UWAI crash in games with minor civs.
    
    Relaxed a rule that had made the AI embargo trade value a lower bound for the AI war trade value. [advc.104o]
    
    --
    USER INTERFACE
    
    "Clock" tab of the BUG menu renamed to "Time". [advc.067]
    
    New option on the "Time" tab for switching the game year between AD prefix (AdvCiv default), AD postfix (BtS behavior) and CE/BCE [advc.002k]
    
    Moved AdvCiv's promotion glow option [advc.002e] from GlobalDefines to the "Unit Icons" tab of the BUG menu. And showing the glow after loading wasn't working quite correctly; fixed.
    
    Replaced the "Gold Rate Warning" option ("General" tab) with three dropdown menus that set the color of the gold rate when it's positive, negative or negative and exceeding the reserves in the treasury. One can now e.g. use yellow for a positive gold rate – I was going to do that, but it looks a bit too unfamiliar, so the defaults remain as in BtS. [advc.070]
    
    Replaced some of the color options in the BUG menu with similar, but more frequently used (text) colors, e.g. COLOR_HIGHLIGHT_TEXT instead of COLOR_CYAN. As a side-effect, many BUG color settings will, regrettably, revert to the default value when updating to AdvCiv v0.95. [advc.004]
    
    Darkened the green of the research bar a bit. [advc.002i]
    
    When anarchy starts, choose-research popups are killed and re-launched when anarchy ends. (Choose-production popups had already been treated that way.) During anarchy and before any city is founded, the BASE_RESEARCH_RATE (of 1 research/turn) doesn't apply. No choose-tech buttons are shown on the research bar when the research rate is 0 and no turns-to-research prediction is shown. [advc.004x]
    
    The research rate shown on the main interface includes the 1 beaker from BASE_RESEARCH_RATE. (BtS shows only the research from city commerce.) [advc.004x]
    
    When progress is gained on a tech (e.g. from a goody hut) while a choose-tech popup is minimized, the popup is relaunched with updated turns-to-research info. [advc.004x]
    
    "Obsolete with" info for buildings shows only the name of the technology in red (not the words "Obsolete with") – unless the building is already obsolete (then all in red as in BtS). [advc.004w]
    
    The UI never shows damaged units at full strength nor at 0.0 strength. E.g. a Warrior with 98/100 hitpoints is shown with strength 1.9/2 instead of 2.0/2 (exact value: 1.96/2). [advc.004]
    
    BUG FoodAssist option again disabled by default. Too distracting. [advc.004]
    
    K-Mod shortcut [X] for suppressing unit cycling added to Shortcuts section of Civilopedia. [advc.004y]
    
    --
    BUGFIXES AND REFACTORING
    
    Fixed an inconsistency between BaseGreatPeopleRate and GreatPeopleUnitRate in Barbarian cities with wonders or specialists. (I've only encountered this problem in the Earth1000AD scenario, which places Chichen Itza in a Barbarian city, but I suppose it could also be an issue if Barbarians capture a wonder.) [advc.051]
    
    Attitude cache and (K-Mod) commerce weights are no longer updated for Barbarians. And some other shortcuts for Barbarians in the AI code. [advc.003n]
    
    Fixed an issue with [advc.127b] (adds jump-to locations to most announcement messages, usually the location of a capital): Must attach only locations that are revealed.
    (While clicking on a message in the Event Log has no effect if the attached location is unrevealed, the EXE also shows a flashing dot on the minimap when displaying the message, without double-checking whether the location is revealed.)
    
    Fixed an issue with the "Open Event Log" option: The log hadn't been opening along with stop-trading diplo popups. [advc.106b]
    
    Fixed an inconsistency in [advc.026] (gold offered by the AI): When asked to make a proposal, the AI had only sometimes rounded gold to a multiple of 5; now it always does.
    
    Help text for Temple shows that Priesthood is required. (This "special building" tech requirement was somehow missing in CvGameTextMgr::buildBuildingRequiresString.) [advc.004w]

commit b9397691e4d045403bce7d920fa14b401c8c4448
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jan 11 23:28:53 2019 +0100

    AI contacts human players to sue for peace or capitulate
    
    Finally got [advc.134a] to work. It's a workaround for the bug in the EXE that prevents AI-to-human peace offers from being shown. CvTeam::isAtWar now feigns peace at just the right moment to stop the EXE from discarding the peace offer. The downside is that, to ensure the proper order of isAtWar calls, CvPlayer::canContact and CvPlayer::canTradeItem now have to call a different function (CvTeam::isAtWarInternal, with ::atWar in CvGameCoreUtils as an alias) to check at-war status. And, in terms of the challenge posed by the AI, the peace offers (which have to include a discount to be worth considering) can only hurt the AI against a competent player.
    
    I've made a couple of adjustments to the timing of AI peace offers and the items that are demanded or offered. In particular, I changed the ContactRand values (was 1 chance in 20 for all leaders) and ContactDelay (was 10 turns for all leaders) of some AI leaders:
    Delay decreased to 5: Gandhi
    Delay increased to 15: Boudica, Sitting Bull, Tokugawa
    Rand decreased to 10: Gandhi
    Rand decreased to 12: Mansa Musa, Pacal, Joao, Hatshepsut, Ashoka, Huayna Capac
    Rand decreased to 15 for 17 of the 52 leaders.
    These timing values only affect AI-to-human peace if UWAI is enabled; otherwise (legacy AI), ContactRand also affects peace deals between AI civs.
    
    This commit will be difficult to test properly because AI Auto Play doesn't help with AI-to-human offers.
    
    I've moved some K-Mod code for creating AI proposals around to avoid code duplication; hopefully no functional difference. [advc.003]
    
    Fixed a bug in [advc.001e] (cancellation of outdated AI defensive pact offers and stop-trading demands): wrong order of remove and delete calls.
    
    In Debug mode, holding down [Alt] while hovering over a leader portrait shows the leader's id (player slot number). [advc.007]
    
    Plus a little bit of random refactoring in CvCityAI.cpp and CvGame.cpp.

commit bd47281d75e600ef0e08dff0fffdd853fbacf536
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Dec 28 23:11:54 2018 +0100

    More UI/accessibility changes (mostly; big commit)
    
    Let's start with:
    Changes not (directly) related to the BUG menu:
    * Fixed an issue with [advc.001c]: No GP probabilities had been shown when there was a positive GP rate but no accumulated progress yet.
    * Bug fixed in the recently merged [dlph.26] (restructured code for triggered declarations of war): Attitude cache was not getting updated when there was just a single declaration of war (no wars triggered).
    * Added an upper bound for the number of Barbarians placed per unowned tile because Barbarian activity was sometimes too intense on the highest difficulty settings. [advc.300]
    (Still to be done: When placing Barbarians, take into account where Barbarians have previously been placed or killed. This mechanism is going make sure that Barbarians don't keep coming and coming in large numbers.)
    * Animals may enter unowned tiles with a resource if that resource requires a tech to be revealed. This should make it impossible to infer hidden resources from the movements of animals. [advc.309]
    * Default number of Advanced Start points in the Ancient era set to 400 (was 800). 400 is a better default for the SPaH option and not unreasonable for regular Advanced Start. [advc.250b]
    * Two bugs fixed in BUG's calculateTradeRoutes function (TradeUtil.py). I don't think either of these had any impact in AdvCiv, but they were still bugs. Merged from Dawn of Civilization; Git commit:
    https://github.com/dguenms/Dawn-of-Civilization/commit/6dbe19867e7f398b1a4922fdf6dd9492e0a9b9b9
    * Freed up some space on the "Active" tab of the Foreign Advisor by removing the leader name headings. [advc.066]
    * To make the help text shown when hovering over a unit icon more compact, the owner is no longer shown when the unit belongs to the active player.  [advc.069]
    * Colon removed after "Turn" on the game turn display (upper right corner). [advc.002k]
    * Sevopedia shows icons before category headings only if there is room. In English, almost all headings are sufficiently short, but, in other languages, many are too long (given the AdvCiv font size). [advc.002b]
    * A few more changes to the shortcuts section of Sevopedia. [advc.004y]
    
    As a result of trying to generate some very large maps:
    * Amended [advc.030] (impassable tiles can separate map areas) to make the computation of areas less memory-intensive.
    * Fixed a Python crash at game start resulting from [advc.004a] (reworked bulb path utility). In the process, I've exposed CvGlobalContext::IsGraphicsInitialized to Python. I'm keeping it exposed although I'm not using it after all.
    
    BUG MENU
    
    Tidied up the layout of the entire BUG/K-Mod menu, in part, to match AdvCiv's increased font size [advc.002b], revised or rewrote most of the help texts (some of which were nearly incomprehensible to me) in English and German and made minor changes to the behavior of some of the options, in particular, again, changes to help text (on the actual widgets). Merged a bit of code from BULL, but nothing major; some of that remains to be done (see Tbd. in the manual under change id 004). The one part of BUG that I mostly skipped is the Customizable Domestic Advisor.
    
    Improved the handling of invalid data in BUG ini files. Hopefully, this will later result in smooth updates from AdvCiv 0.94 to 0.95. [advc.009d]
    In the process, I came across a few bugs in the error handling code in BugOptionsTab.py. [advc.001]
    
    BUG no longer writes default values and hover text as comments into its ini files. As far as I can tell, this only affects new installations because the comments are only written once when the ini files are created -- which is also why I'm disabling them: they become outdated when the options-related XML files are changed. (And the ini files shouldn't be edited manually anyway, so comments don't make much sense.) [advc.009d]
    
    AdvCiv options moved from XML to the BUG menu (enabled by default):
    * Option to show resource bubbles at the start of a new game moved to the "Map" tab. Also, the option didn't actually work. I think it did work in v0.94 and I don't know how I broke it, but, anyway, it should be fixed now. [advc.004m]
    * Option to color-code team membership moved to the "Score" tab. Now only works when the option for the Advanced/Tabular layout is also enabled. [advc.155]
    * Moved the "List Units per Owner" option [advc.061] from the General tab of the BUG menu to the Map tab. [advc.061]
    
    Merged from BULL:
    * Adapted WhipAssist (overflow info on Hurry button) to K-Mod's treatment of excess overflow. Overflow info on the production bar (if enabled) now uses the same (C++) code as WhipAssist; redundant Python code in CvMainInterface.py commented out. [advc.064]
    
    Functional changes to BUG options:
    * Uncoupled the "Show Era" and "Show Era Color" options from the "Just Another Game Clock" option and rearranged the "Clock" tab a bit. Added an option to show the primary view of the clock for a longer or shorter time period than the alternate view. (Also added an option for showing the game era instead of the active player's era, but then changed my mind and hid the new option through BugNJAGCOptionsTab.py.) [advc.067]
    * Added a dirty-bit for the Tech Advisor screen so that the tech tree gets properly redrawn when era colors are changed. [advc.068]
    * Some changes to PLE mode/filter button help text to match the terminology of the menu. [advc.069]
    * PLE help text for unit icons shows only the basic unit help; had previously shown e.g. the unique replacements of the unit and its production cost. Turns to heal now shown on a separate line (was an inscrutable number after the combat strength values). [advc.069]
    * PLE bugfixes: [advc.001,advc.069]
    - Movement Highlighter had crashed sometimes (AStarTools.py).
    - Color changes to unit bars had only been applied after a restart (PlotListEnhancements.py).
    - Health bars had been shown for civilian units (PLE.py; possibly intended that way).
    * "Fractional Movement Points" now also affects the help text shown when hovering over a unit icon in the plot list. [advc.069]
    * Bugs fixed in the Autolog mod (autologEventManager.py): had assumed in a few places that the active player is in slot 0, which isn't usually true in scenarios. I haven't tested the corrections in a scenario, so perhaps there are further issues. [advc.001]
    
    Removed BUG options:
    * "Show Strategy layer" because players can use Ctrl+X for that
    * "Show Percent Progress" (game clock) because the percentage of elapsed game turns isn't a helpful statistic.
    * Option for setting the default counting method for Raw Yields
    * "Pending: Border Expansion" and "Peace" alerts
    * Dark gray can no longer be selected in BUG's drop-down menus. Orange can be selected instead.
    * Blinking reminder about the BUG menu shortcut
    * Start year setting (Autolog); the log always uses game turn and game year now.
    * "Show Culture Turns", "Commerce Subtotals", "Widescreen" (Tech Advisor) and K-Mod's "Non-Zero Stats Only" are always enabled, no longer optional. [advc.065]
    
    Changes to default settings:
    (applies only to new installations of AdvCiv)
    * "Improved Info Tab" disabled (tab "Advisors")
    * Send reminders as popups (was popup AND on-screen message; tab "Alerts")
    * Show WhipAssist tooltip on the hurry button (previously unavailable; tab "City Screen")
    * FoodAssist ("Detailed Food Info") enabled (tab "City Screen")
    * Promotion indicator for unit icons disabled (tab "Unit Icons" tab)
    These changes are only relevant if one enables other options that remain disabled by default:
    * Promotion Offset in PLE help text set to 8 in order to match changes to the size of the text pane (was 0; tab "Unit Icons")
    * Custom Inland Advisor's color-coding disabled (tab "Advisors")
    * "Health Bars" for unit icons enabled and hidden during combat (tab "Unit Icons")
    * Don't record reminders through Autolog (tab "Alerts")
    * Don't record slider positions through Autolog (tab "Autolog")
    * To reduce the space taken up by the "alternate" info of Advanced Combat Odds:
    - "Survival Odds" and "Unharmed Odds" are never shown
    - "Basic Values" are only shown in standard view, not in alternate
    - "XP Range" never shown, alternate view shows "Unrounded XP" instead

Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    UI support for partial worker builds added
    
    If Ctrl is held down while issuing a command to a Worker, the build is stopped one turn before completion. ("pre-build")
    
    If Ctrl is held down while hovering over a tile, the progress on all unfinished builds is shown.
    
    These additions address the following open K-Mod issue:
    https://github.com/karadoc/Civ4-K-Mod/issues/1
    (Now that I've amended this commit twice, I realize that I shouldn't have included the Issue link. GitHub has pinned each of my amendments to the Issue. Sorry.)
    
    I've taken up boeti's suggestion (or maybe I had the same thought independently) with the modifier key.
    My implementation is safe for multiplayer - in principle, I've only done one quick test. The whole thing isn't properly tested yet.
    
    Progress on unfinished builds still decays through change [advc.011] if the tile is left alone for too long. "Too long" is now 8 turns; was 5 turns before.
    
    I've adopted some code from BULL. (Can't find out the specific author.) These adoptions are marked with [advc.011c], whereas my original code is marked with [advc.011b].

commit 470df8df939b720d8fab879baccfb23c0b093ce2
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Dec 22 22:59:07 2018 +0100

    Changes to handicap settings to improve balance and pace, and some misc. changes
    
    Changes to Civ4HandicapInfos.xml (see manual for details): [advc.251]
    
    * On Emperor difficulty and above, human civs pay higher production costs and face higher city growth and GP thresholds. AI production discounts have been lowered. Added a new AI discount that lowers GP thresholds on Monarch difficulty and above. These changes should make the various yields more balanced and reduce the number of units on the map.
    * Human production costs, research costs and GP thresholds are rounded to the nearest multiple of 5.
    * Replaced the multiplicative per-era modifier for AI discounts with an additive modifier based on the game turn number. The new modifier applies to AI production costs, research costs and city growth thresholds. (Whereas the per-era modifier had applied to production costs, city growth thresholds, expenses and war weariness. An earlier change [advc.250d] had already uncoupled AI upgrade costs and unit supply from the per-era modifier.)
    * (Human) civic upkeep increased on all difficulty levels below Monarch; now the same progression as inflation. Increased the AI civic upkeep and unit cost modifiers on Deity from 60% to 75% (meaning that the Deity AI has to pay higher civic upkeep and unit cost than in BtS).
    
    The BBAI era modifier for tech costs (Civ4EraInfos.xml) is now actually applied to tech costs; was previously applied to research rates. [advc.910]
    Likewise, the AdvCiv adjustments for the "No Tech Trading" [advc.550d] and "Raging Barbarians" [advc.308] game options now apply to tech costs instead of research rates.
    No research bonus for knowing a single prereq tech. I've instead reduced all tech costs by about 20% through the era modifier. [advc.910]
    Changed the game year computation on Normal speed so that the years pass a bit faster in Renaissance. This should match the historical time line better. [advc.910]
    Tech cost of Iron Working increased a little. [advc.031b]
    
    Changes to free units on the highest two difficulty levels: [advc.250e]
    * Reduced the number of free Archers that the AI receives at game start by 1 on Immortal and Deity difficulty.
    * Reduced the number of defensive units placed in Barbarian cities from 4 to 3 on Immortal difficulty.
    
    AI floating defenders are no longer double adjusted to the AI cost discounts. I had added such an adjustment as part of [advc.107] without realizing that it was redundant.
    
    Three changes inspired by this post and the next by Akbarthegreat in the K-Mod subforum:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/k-mod-far-beyond-the-sword.407049/page-149#post-15311568
    * When the AI cancels a vassal agreement, the diplo text states the reason (e.g. "we're doing fine on our own now"). [advc.062]
    * When a civ is close to a Domination victory, vassals of that civ which are Pleased with their master don't break away, even if their power rating is above the global average. [advc.112]
    * Bad terrain is never replaced under a precious resource (Gold/Silver/Gems) and a bad feature on a precious resource is only removed in the inner ring around the starting location. [advc.108]
    
    Slightly decreased the size of the Modern Armor 3D model. [advc.002j]
    
    Reworded the help text for the InstanceCostModifier ability, though the ability is still unused. (I could see myself using it for War Elephant.) [advc.004g]
    
    Enabled an assertion in CvXMLLoadUtility that reports when a GetChildXmlValByName call fails. This reveals typos in the CvInfos::read(CvXMLLoadUtility*) functions, which can otherwise easily go undetected. [advc.006b]
    
    Const qualifier added to several CvMap functions. [advc.003]
    
    Added a check in the InvasionGraph class (UWAI) to prevent a crash when playing from an old (pre-v0.93?) savegame.
    
    Some refactoring in CvGameTextMgr::setTechHelp. [advc.003]

commit 662e020a56765e5df4cee3ac8769079829d61cb4
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Dec 22 13:07:25 2018 +0100

    Tentative changes to make naval invasions easier to intercept
    
    On the turn that war is declared, units that enter enemy borders have all their movement points spent. (Except air units and units that can explore rival territory.) [advc.162]
    
    Units that get "bumped" out of foreign territory have all their movement points spent. They're also woken up and de-automated (if they had e.g. been set to auto-explore). {advc.163]
    
    Drill I enables the Blitz promotion, but Blitz allows only one extra attack per turn (was previously limited only by the unit's movement points).  [advc.164]
    
    Fixed some issues with routes in the fog of war that I came across while implementing the above:
    The pathfinder waypoints no longer give away unrevealed routes on revealed tiles, and the tile danger computations of the AI respect fog of war for routes. [advc.001i]

commit cbb4852bb0a72aefb11307b1c0ef18dfffcc310c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Dec 16 23:07:31 2018 +0100

    Cppcheck (refactoring, minor bugfixes), bugs fixed in naval AI
    
    Ran the whole DLL code base through Cppcheck (code analysis) and went through the ca. 1000 (style) warnings. A lot of these were clearly not worth addressing (e.g. constructors with single arguments) or false positives. The ones I did address were mostly shadowed variables, redundant code and "scope can be reduced," resulting from the C-style variable declarations at the start of a function. I've moved most of the declarations that Cppcheck objected to because they had been bothering me for some time. Most of these stylistic changes I haven't marked in the code because that would defeat the purpose of making the code easier read. [advc.003i]
    
    Unused functions and classes: I've left the majority of these alone (apart from adding a comment), but some I've commented out, removed through the preprocessor or deleted. [advc.003j]
    
    While I've come across a few dozen apparent oversights, very few of these had actually resulted in erroneous behavior, and the few that did, look like very minor bugs: [advc.001]
    - CvPlayerAI::AI_doDiplo: A mixup of two variables had made the AI reluctant to give away more than one technology in an (inter-AI) war trade.
    - CvUnitAI::AI_assaultSeaTransport: In the AI code for choosing the tile to unload on, a condition that discourages unloading on the wrong side of a river had had no effect.
    - Fractal.cpp::tectonicAction: This looks like two variables were mixed up, but I'm not sure that my version is correct either. The code is used (only?) by the Continents map script.
    
    Unrelated to the above, I've encountered and fixed several issues in the naval AI resulting from [advc.017b] (and BBAI code) that had sometimes caused the AI to train way too many Galleys on certain maps (especially Pangaea).
    
    While I was at it: The AI now trains fewer sea explorers (typically just 1 instead of 2) if the map script's file name is "Pangaea". [advc.017]

commit b62c4000571695a9d6ccc5c462fd606f4f172d33
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Dec 12 13:13:59 2018 +0100

    XML cache disabled
    [advc.003i]
    
    It appears that the cache is never written when a mod is loaded, meaning that the cache accomplishes nothing and the write/read attempts only waste time (though probably very little). On top of that, it's possible that, in rare cases, cache data written by the unmodded game is read by the mod, which will result in errors.
    
    Credit to Nightinggale for telling me me how to disable it:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/avoid-creating-bugs-from-the-exe-calling-the-dll.639167/#post-15297196

    CFC user vedg reported the bug here:

commit d4fd8b627725487982f600b0f7f9327fa3756119
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Nov 20 13:41:52 2018 +0100

    More stop-trading tweaks, UI tweaks (combat odds, animations, city alerts), a few minor bugfixes (AdvCiv,K-Mod)
    
    Stop-trading resolutions (UN, AP) cancel recently signed deals, and such deals don't prevent the resolution from being proposed. Exception: The civ that proposes the resolution mustn't have deals with the target that are too recent to be canceled.
    AI civs vote against the resolution if they have deals that are too recent. [advc.130f]
    (This behavior is consistent with the changes to war resolutions [dlph.25] in a previous commit and is consistent with regular embargoes canceling recently signed deals.)
    
    The AI refuses to stop trading ("not right now") when this would cancel reparations paid for a peace treaty. [advc.130f]
    
    Amended AI refusal to stop trading: No longer fear the "military might" of a vassal. [advc.130f]
    
    Bug (sign error) fixed in a recent change to attitude thresholds for embargoes. [advc.130f]
    
    Fixed a (likely) UI bug in K-Mod code that had sometimes caused a neutral unit to be shown on the map instead of an enemy unit when neutral and enemy units occupied the same tile (making the enemy unit easy to miss). [advc.001]
    
    Fixed a problem with oscillation of tile ownership in [advc.099b].
    For performance reasons, the total culture in a tile is now stored in savegames and a function getTotalCulture replaces countTotalCulture in the CvPlot class. [advc.003b]
    
    Improved the AI evaluation of deals where the AI receives two health resources or two happiness resources from a human. (The AI still refuses to trade more than two.) [advc.036]
    
    Changes to combat odds help text: [advc.048]
    * Odds help text shows which unit (short description incl. current and maximal strength and promotions) is about to defend and, if multiple units are selected, which one is about to attack.
    * Hitpoints of the combatants are no longer shown separately.
    * Advanced Combat Odds (ACO) already had options for showing the attacking and defending unit. These are now enabled by default. ACO is still disabled by default.
    * Replaced a few uses of the word "retreat" with "withdraw" in combat odds and other help text. ("Withdraw" is the proper term.)
    
    Combat animations become shorter with each era. Configurable through GlobalDefinesAlt.xml. [advc.002m]
    
    Fixed an oversight in AdvCiv code that had prevented the declare-war popup from appearing when a player attempted to attack an enemy unit on the territory of a non-friendly third party. [advc.001]
    
    The "pending" alerts only trigger when a negative event is about to happen: when a city is about to become unhappy or unhealthy or is about to shrink. About-to-become-unhappy now enabled by default (this only affects new installations of AdvCiv). [advc.106d]

commit a8a7e75c6cde190a0d71297d80ca8f68d064faa0
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Nov 17 17:51:06 2018 +0100

    Some bugfixes (in K-Mod, Kek-Mod, AdvCiv code)
    
    Fixed issues with [dlph.25]: It seems that war votes against a voting member of the AP had been impossible because the game was checking if all voting members - including the war target - were able to declare war. This is now only checked for full members, only full members declare war when the resolution passes and only full members can defy a war vote. Moreover, only peace treaties of the AP leader can block war votes, i.e. the AP overrules peace treaties of other members. An AI civ that has a peace treaty with the target will try to honor the treaty by voting against the war.
    
    Fixed a K-Mod bug in CvPlayerAI::AI_baseBonusVal. The AI had failed to recognize units as obsolete when evaluating a strategic resource that it didn't have access to yet. This had sometimes led the AI to cancel and renew trades for strategic resources (especially Horse) every 10 turns. [advc.001u]
    
    A trade embargo sets stopped-trading-recent memory to 2 rather than adding 2, meaning that multiple embargoes don't stack. [advc.130f]
    
    Amended [advc.106f] so that a canceled defensive pact is no longer doubly announced to the civ that cancels it.
    
    "No Random Events" enabled by default. [advc.104z]
    
    For debugging the UWAI component: Added a function WarAndPeaceAI::Team::doWarReport.

commit 459038215daf879fade2510cc8d3aae4de4ebee8
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Nov 14 19:36:25 2018 +0100

    AI tweaks: embargoes, Barbarian unit AI, defying AP peace
    
    Changes to trade embargoes: [advc.130f]
    * Changed my mind again about embargo duration: Now 18 turns on average (15 in a recent commit, 22 in v0.93, 30 in BtS).
    * When a war ends, stopped-trading-recently memory of all war parties is reduced to 1, meaning that embargoed war parties become willing to trade, on average, 9 turns after the war ends.
    * The threshold for the AI attitude toward the embargo target can be decreased by one level if the attitude toward the player who proposes the embargo is one level higher than required (i.e., in most cases, when Friendly). The AI still won't stop trading when Pleased with the target.
    * AI refuses to stop trading with civs that pose an immediate danger: "We're afraid of their military might". And I've increased the impact of power ratio on the embargo trade value.
    * Embargo trade value takes into account the number of civs in the game (an embargo is more consequential when there are few civs to trade with).
    
    Fixed an issue introduced with [advc.106d]: The willing-to-talk alert had not been shown when an embargo ended at peacetime.
    
    Small adjustment to the relations penalty for enemy trade: When a non-war party trades with a war enemy, the AI gets upset even if relations with the non-war party are already (almost) as bad as relations with the war enemy. (Previously, to prevent the worst enemy from oscillating, trades between civs that the AI disliked equally had been ignored. Generally, that's still the case; punishing outside help for a war enemy is more important though.) [advc.130p]
    
    Improved the AI code for defying AP resolutions. Was previously only based on war utility, now takes into account the number of cities with the AP religion. Still doesn't check if the anger from defying would actually cause problems. [advc.104n]
    
    Tentatively fixed a K-Mod issue (perhaps also broken in BtS) where the AI declared war without immediately crossing the border. [advc.001t]
    
    Warlords bug fixed: Barbarians no longer target cities protected by the Great Wall. [advc.001]
    
    Simplified the part of change [advc.300] that deals with AI attacks against Barbarian cities, and refactored the part that deals with the behavior of Barbarian attackers. Fixed an oversight that had caused Barbarian units spawned on small continents to behave unaggressively.

Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    Balance changes to some ships and a few misc. changes
    
    Ship of the Line requires Iron again (K-Mod had made Copper an alternative), gets +25% vs. Frigate (was 20% in K-Mod, 50% in BtS), +1 speed with Coal and costs 110 production (was 120). I've added a unit ability "SpeedBonuses" to the XML schema for this purpose. [advc.905b]

Withdrawal chance is again 50% (was 60% in earlier AdvCiv versions). Stealth Destroyer receives the same anti-air and anti-submarine abilities as Destroyer and 1 cargo space for missiles, but also a cost increase from 220 to 270 and has its strength decreased to 30 (same as in BtS; was 33 in earlier AdvCiv versions and 36 in K-Mod). [advc.906]
