    Amended my code for AI strike avoidance after realizing that the strike counter isn't reset in between strikes. [advc.131]
    
    Bug fixed in AI deal proposals: After balancing a deal out with gold per turn, the AI had not always realized that the deal was square and had asked for an additional item (e.g. a technology). I think this is also broken in K-Mod, but probably matters very rarely because K-Mod makes less gold per turn available for trade than AdvCiv. [advc.001]
    
    UWAI:
    * Increased the negative war utility counted for ill will from militarily powerful partners of the war target.
    * Increased the granularity of the score remembered by the AI at the end of a war. The duration of the war is now taken into account in addition to war successes.
    
    Pillaged improvements are announced immediately (bForce=true). [advc.106j]
    
    Tweaked the 3D model sizes of ships. [advc.002j]

    Bugfixes in naval AI; reduced UWAI dogpiling; diplo decay tweaked

    One of these oversights (in K-Mod code) seems to have caused AI ships to ignore hostile units in AI_retreatToCity. I've written some new code that flags cities as safe or (potentially) unsafe at the start of an AI turn. Idle ships are never moved into unsafe cities; the AI keeps ships at sea if no city is safe.     Deal cancelation during an AI turn is only immediately announced if it's an open borders agreement, defensive pact or peace treaty, or if a resource trade was canceled by the game rules (trade network severed); regular cancelation of gold and resource deals isn't announced until the start of the next human turn. [advc.106j]

commit 82ed992626a03f21b42345058cfdea526337641e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 7 08:11:59 2018 +0200

    AI improvements, mostly related to naval war
    (This commit contains some temporary code (marked with advc.tmp) that suppresses change advc.122, which is still work in progress.)
    
    Minor (tentative) changes to the AI routines for picking up stranded units, and the game tries (but not very hard) to bump units to a landmass where their owner has a city. [advc.046]
    Prompted by this CFC thread:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/k-mod-bugs.637116/
    Also fixed a bug in civics evaluation mentioned there, [advc.001]
    and civics are now adopted probabilistically, as had already been the case for religions in AdvCiv. [advc.031]
    
    Made AI less likely to raze the first city conquered on another continent if there is a good chance of conquering further cities on that continent. And some refactoring. [advc.116]
    
    UWAI:
    * Revised earlier changes to AI preparations for naval vs. land war.
    * Increased impact of the victory-related WarUtilityAspects in the early game. In particular, stage 2 of the Conquest and Domination victory strategies can increase war utility now. (These victory stages had already made the K-Mod AI more warlike, but UWAI had so far only cared about stages 3 and 4.)
    * Fixed an issue with AI civs dogpiling on a far stronger opponent when that opponent was already Furious at the dogpile attacker.
    * Fixed a bug introduced in v0.93: Military power had been grossly underestimated when a defending civ had cities on several landmasses and a lot of Mounted or other fast units.
    * Made the AI a little more optimistic about future uses for the military units that it expects to train for a war. Personality (BuildUnitProb) also matters a bit now. This change makes the AI a bit less worried about the cost of military build-up and a bit more worried about casualties.
    * Fixed issues that had prevented the AI from starting a war by invading a vassal.  [advc.104j]
    
    Debug mode: Exiting the Civics screen after switching to the perspective of another civ can no longer change the civics of the human civ. [advc.001]
    
    Merged from the Dawn of Civilization mod:
    "Minor civs cannot be involved as the other player in events" [advc.001]
    https://github.com/dguenms/Dawn-of-Civilization/commit/d5313deda8960c63f3a1ab755961be64cb2f7e80

    Minor changes to AI war preparations and AI espionage
    
    UWAI [advc.104s]:

commit 20a48bbe1590699f79702bdf57c7059faf35cae6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Sep 30 16:06:46 2018 +0200

    Last batch of misc. changes (toward v0.94)
    (barely tested so far)
    
    Flood Plains are only placed orthogonally adjacent to rivers, not on river bends. [advc.129b]
    
    Quechua loses its bonus against Archers and costs 15 (was 20 in K-Mod). [advc.907b]
    
    Heal rate in cities under occupation reduced from 20 HP/turn to 15 (same as in friendly non-city tiles). [advc.023]
    
    When the AI asks a player for help, it asks for the technology that it needs most instead of a random technology. [advc.144]
    
    Revised AI trade value modifiers for technologies in Civ4TechInfos.xml. (These modifiers make the AI charge or pay 10% extra when trading certain technologies.) [advc.552]
    
    "No Tech Brokering" no longer causes the AI to reject tech trades stating "We would have nothing to gain".
    (Change 550e allows techs received in trade to be traded despite the no-brokering option if the recipient already had 67% progress when receiving the tech. Therefore, the nothing-to-gain answer is no longer needed.)
    
    If the no-war probability from Civ4LeaderHeadInfos.xml would be 100 for a civ that the AI doesn't have Open Borders with, the AI computes its no-war probability as if its attitude toward the other civ was one level lower than it actually is. This should allow the AI to attack a human neighbor despite good relations if the human closes his or her borders so that the AI can't reach any other target. [advc.104y]
    
    UWAI prediction of unit upgrades takes into account stockpiled gold (previously only based on GNP curve).
    
    Cleaned up change advc.104i (This should make practically no functional difference.) MEMORY_STOPPED_TRADING_RECENT is no longer used for keeping track of recently declared wars; a new AI memory type MEMORY_DECLARED_WAR_RECENT is used instead. [advc.104i]
    
    When two civs make peace, both become willing to talk to any remaining war parties. E.g. in the case of a triggered Defensive Pact, the two allies refuse to talk for some (randomized) amount of time in order to honor the Defensive Pact. If the first ally to become willing to talk made peace, previously, the other ally might have continued to refuse to talk. [advc.104i]
    
    Some changes to random events that can start or end a war. These are just band-aids; a proper overhaul of random events would be a big task -- not worth it to me.
    * When the AI gets the Great Mediator or Heroic Gesture event, it offers peace only with a 33% probability (was 50%). [advc.104z]
    * Bug fixed in the BtS evaluation of AI responses to events: When a response causes a relations penalty, an unfavorable power ratio can make the BtS AI more inclined to pick this response; now power ratio has the opposite effect. This bugfix should make it unlikely that the AI provokes a catastrophic war through the Wedding Feud event. [advc.104z]
    * When a war is ended through a random event, the replay log records this. (Wars started through an event had already been recorded in v0.93.) [advc.106g]
    
    Expired peace treaties are canceled at the start of a round. Previously, they were canceled at the end of a turn, so a player who wanted to declare war right after the treaty expired had to cancel the peace deal manually. [advc.004]
    
    Declarations of war on and by non-human vassals are never accompanied by the war-horn sound. And no sound when a non-human vassal makes peace.
    If the Event Log is opened at the start of a turn (i.e. > 3 messages), declarations of war on or by a vassal and peace treaties with vassals are no longer shown on the main interface unless the active player is directly involved. [advc.106b]
    
    Unit layer option "Non-military" renamed to "Civilians" (originally was "Domestics"). [advc.004z]
    
    City name changes are recorded in replays. The game checks only at the end of each turn if the name has changed; i.e. changing a name multiple times or back and forth doesn't mess up the replay. [advc.106k]
    
    Start and end of AI Auto Play are recorded in replays. [advc.127]
    
    Rise & Fall option:
    * Fixed a bug that had caused the AI to respond with "We can't accept gifts" even when trade was not restricted. [advc.705]
    * Trade is restricted with civs that are ranked lower on the scoreboard than the player (previously: civs in the lower half); and the game era no longer matters. [advc.705]
    * The start of an intermediate period between chapters is recorded in replays. [advc.706]
    
    Some random refactoring. [advc.003]
    
    Draft of future gameplay changes updated.

commit 5473a1906a6f5ba6b9daeddac3d3d1eafbe9bd74
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Sep 29 01:09:55 2018 +0200

    Relations modifiers from trade further tweaked:
    [advc.130p]
    * Better adjusted to difficulty (modifiers were too high on medium and low difficulty settings), game speed and map size.
    * Diminishing returns: It's harder to get from e.g. +3 to +4 "fair and forthright" trade than from 0 to +1.
    * The AI subtracts 5/6 of the value that the other side receives instead of subtracting 100%. This means trades that are indeed "fair" contribute a bit to the fair-trade bonus.
    * Now based on asset values at the time of the trade instead of game score.
    
    Minor changes to AI asset values: Values of techs read from XML are reduced to 75%. [advc.131]
    
    AI evaluation of extra trade routes from tech takes future cities into account. Currency is probably still underrated by the AI, but it's a step in the right direction. [advc.131]

commit 20d7ef5a94cf7377c1f6415d0370e3c54919037d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Sep 24 00:58:38 2018 +0200

    Rival-trade penalties, war trades on Glance tab, misc. changes:
    
    Rival-trade memory ("you've traded with our worst enemy"): [advc.130p]
    * Trades with a war enemy increase rival-trade memory even if that war enemy is not the worst enemy, though not as much as trades with the worst enemy do.
    * Payments in peace deals increase rival-trade memory. Payments by a third party (brokered peace) are tolerated by civs that are Pleased with the civ with whom peace has been made. Payments in two-party peace deals count only partially for rival-trade memory.
    * Annual trades (resources, gold per turn) are no longer double counted for trade memory during the first 10 turns.
    * (Only relevant for mod-mods: The relations modifier is multiplied by MemoryAttitudePercent-EVENT_BAD_TO_US. This is set to 100% in Civ4LeaderHeadInfos.xml for every leader.)
    
    The Glance tab shows a fist icon when a leader is willing to declare war on another leader. [advc.152]
    
    Only one free AI Scout on Emperor difficulty (was 2). [advc.250e]
    
    Hopefully fixed a problem with city names not appearing in announcements about diplo votes. [advc.150b]
    
    PerfectMongoose: The Old World Starts option reserves the second largest continent for the New World only if this leaves enough room in the Old World; otherwise, smaller continents are reserved. [advc.021b]
    
    Barbarians can no longer train or receive Cavalry, Anti-Tank and SAM Infantry. Musketman remains the only post-Medieval unit for Barbarians. The others had mattered too rarely and Barbarian MANPADS and bazookas were too jarring. [advc.307]
    
    Minor changes in AI_unitValue to distinguish AI preferences for City Counter, City Special and Paradrop units more. [advc.005a]

commit 836c1f898279224590e020d7880eb625b9c700ee

commit aa344656f656fda18d6175885be36707f857f263
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Sep 11 02:14:05 2018 +0200

    AI changes, bugfixes, goody hut tweaks
    
    I've realized that BtS didn't have any diplomatic handicap for human players (the penalty on Noble and above applied to human and AI civs alike), meaning that the bonus to inter-AI relations ("first impression") in AdvCiv is a novelty. Updated the v0.93 manual (start of DDiplo chapter) to reflect this. Going forward (v0.93b), I'm reducing the bonus to 0.3 on difficulty settings up to Noble. Above Noble, the bonus increases gradually from 0.4 (Prince) to 0.9 (Deity).
    
    UWAI:
    * Fixed problems in distance measurements between cities; AI had been underestimating long distances a lot. And an earlier performance tweak hadn't really been working; now that it is working, large maps play much faster. (250 turns of AI Auto Play on a Huge map with 18 civs have taken 17 minutes in a test, down from 24 minutes with v0.93.)
    * Refined the computation of the opportunity cost of war; this should sometimes make the AI more willing to start war preparations during the Classical era.
    * Tweaked the formula for weighing limited vs. total war from the previous commit.
    * Military analysis distinguishes between MaxWarNearbyPowerRatio and LimitedWarPowerRatio from LeaderHead XML (had previously used the mean of the two for all non-naval wars). This change increases the impact of AI leader preferences for "limited" vs. "total" war.
    * Slightly Increased the payment expected by an AI civ hired for war by another AI civ when hardly any fighting (or none) has taken place so far. Since v0.93, war allies had been brought in a bit too frequently for my taste.
    * Bug fixed that had caused an AI civ hired for war to continue the war doggedly after the sponsor had made peace. Also, prior to Renaissance, the AI doesn't try to hire AI civs that have no land path to the target or only a very long land path.
    * Bug fixed that had caused the AI to assume a too short preparation time after switching to a different target during war preparations.
    
    The "fair and forthright" relations bonus is adjusted to the map size. Was previously too easy to get on Large and Huge maps. (This probably needs more work, but it's a start.) [advc.130p]
    
    When the AI gets to choose a religion ("Choose Religions" game option), and its favorite isn't available (or it doesn't have a favorite), the AI picks the one with the cheapest tech requirement. (BtS chooses uniformly at random in this case.) [advc.171]
    
    Reduced impact of Growth AI flavor on city placement (Found value). The first few AI cities had been placed a bit too far apart sometimes. [advc.031]
    
    Goody hut tweaks:
    * Increased the probability of free tech at the expense of free gold. (Tech is more interesting than gold and no longer overpowered.) Gold is still a bit likelier than tech. [advc.314]
    * Increased the expected amount of research from 50 to 55 (on Normal speed) and increased the peak turn from 225 to 250. [advc.314]
    * A Scout (or Explorer) entering a hut can't generate another Scout if its owner already has two or more exploration units. [advc.315d]
    * On Epic and Marathon speed: Reduced the grace period in the early game during which no Warrior or free XP can be received. [advc.314]
    
    Barbarian cities flip on the second revolt. (Previously, as in BtS, on the first revolt. Too easy.) [advc.101]
    
    Moved the Resource Layer button so that it's shown at the same position in Globe view as in non-Globe view. And swapped the Bare Map and Show Yields buttons. [advc.004z]
    
    Text for button to toggle gridlines says "Toggle Grid" instead of "Toggle Tiles". [advc.005g]
    
    Fixed typos in theme files that had lead to confusing log output. [advc.002b]
    
    For mod-mods: The "fair and forthright" relations bonus is multiplied by MemoryAttitudePercent-EVENT_GOOD_TO_US in Civ4LeaderHeadInfos.xml. That percentage is 100 for all leaders, but could be modified to make some leaders easier to please through trade than others. [advc.130p]

    Various minor changes
    
    (Not tested much; no DLL committed)
    
    Bug fixed in advc.315a: Scouts had been able to conquer empty cities.
    
    UN and AP don't require Diplo victory to be enabled, but the victory votes do. [advc.178]

The CGS of Mechanized Siege units is now halved through XML instead, and Armored units have the same CGS as in BtS. The latter is now forgotten exactly twice as fast as "you declared war on us" (150 turns) and the former twice as fast as "you razed a holy city" (also 150 turns). [advc.130r]
    
    Tweaked unit AI types (Civ4UnitInfos.xml): Swordsman and Legionary (a.k.a. Praetorian) are City Attackers by default and Battleship gains the (non-default) AI type Escort. [advc.131]
    
    Reduced the impact of personality-based weights on unit types trained by AI cities, increased the impact of personality-based weights for improvements built by the AI (though the impact is still small), and reassigned most of the weights for greater historical accuracy (though the weights still don't work well in that regard) and to avoid boosting unique units too much. [advc.005a]
    
    Made Hinduism Suryavarman's favorite religion because he was a Hindu, not a Buddhist. [advc.005a]
    
    Corrected some info on the "Diplomacy" page in Civilopedia (under "Game Concepts"). [advc.008,advc.130o,advc.104i]

Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

commit a133dd74a0ca49932a3e167cc5fc998c9a33eeb6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Aug 20 09:09:58 2018 +0200

    Changed the way DeclareWarTradeRand (DWTR) is used by the AI.
    
    This value from LeaderHead XML determines the probability of checking for war trades. The probability is now 10 / (DWTR + 10 * min{10,t}), where t is the number of turns that the war has lasted. For small t, the resulting probability is lower than in BtS, and, for large t, it's higher. I might set an individual DWTR value for each leader at a later point; currently they all have DWTR=40 as in BtS. [advc.161]
    
    Revised code for change advc.104i (UWAI willing to talk only according to BtS rules when fighting a war for a third party). Now also applies when an AI civ is paid to start a war, which is what the manual had been saying all along.

commit 69b231572a2f96ffd55352425830a23d7f3fca1d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Aug 18 13:44:11 2018 +0200

    Bugs fixed in AI war trade behavior; tech cost adjustments
    
    Fixed two bugs introduced in the commit from July 31 that had prevented most – if not all – war trades (hired war) between AI civs.
    
    Reduced the price charged by the AI for an embargo by
    * removing some double counting from my formula [advc.130f] and
    * fixing a vanilla Civ 4 bug that was causing all AI trades to be added to the price, not just trades with the target of the embargo. [advc.001q]
    Due to advc.104o, the embargo price also serves as a lower bound for the price for war trades, so these changes also make hired war cheaper.
    
    Increased the cost of an embargo against a militarily powerful civ when the embargo is not part of a war trade. [advc.130f]
    
    "You stopped trading with us" is forgotten after 60 turns on average (same as "You negotiated a trade embargo"). I had missed this one when I set decay rates for all AI memory. [advc.130r]
    
    The extra cost for war trades charged by UWAI to allay suspicions about ulterior motives of the sponsor no longer applies to AI sponsors in most cases, and I've reduced the cost in any case.
    
    Bug fixed in change advc.130p: The AI's worst enemy was sometimes not updated correctly.
    
    Further revised the values in Civ4WorldInfo.xml: [advc.140]
    * Can draft 1 fewer unit per turn on Large and Huge maps.
    * 1 fewer free bonus from the national wonders Broadway, Rock'n'Roll and Hollywood on Standard-size, Large and Huge maps.
    * War weariness increased on Large (now 87%, previously 70%) and Huge maps (now 75%, previously 50%).
    * Minor adjustments to the map-size modifiers for trade route profit, tech costs and distance maintenance.
    
    When Civilopedia is accessed from the main menu, the map-size-based number of draftable units and free bonuses (see above) are shown as a range; e.g. "Nationhood: Can draft 2-4 units per turn". [advc.004y]
    
    Adjusted tech costs to match the changes to AI and rules between v0.92 and 0.93:
    * Increased tech costs in the Classical and Medieval era. [advc.910}
    * Reduced tech costs on Noble difficulty. [advc.251]
    
    As a temporary measure, assigned negative AI weights to Feudalism and Iron Working because the AI had been prioritizing these techs too much. [advc.131b]
    
    DLL and manual (ODT) included, but still being tested.

    Some small AI changes

    * Minor changes to the AI simulations of early mounted attacks that might make the AI more willing to attack across a longer distance with Horse Archers
    * On a similar note, I've increased the impact of MaxWarMinAdjacentLandPercent (MWMALP). commit fb302b8082477c5b59b987f5c1b83d5bd5ad1b84
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 8 19:45:11 2018 +0200

    Various AI tweaks
    
    UWAI:
    * Possibly improved UWAI behavior for starting multiple wars. The AI should now be more likely to end an ongoing war (shortly) before starting a different one.
    * Made the AI less optimistic about getting war enemies to capitulate.
    * Fixed minor issues with the counting of lost units in military simulations and making peace when war utility is near 0 (i.e. when the AI isn't sure whether to make peace).
    
    Diplo values:
    * The AI counting of memory values (e.g. "years of peace") is now adjusted to the game speed setting. (Based on the Growth modifier in the Ancient era, based on the Golden Age modifier in the Medieval era and later, and based on the mean of Growth and Golden Age in the Classical era.) Especially early on, too many relations bonuses had been accumulating (peace, open borders). [advc.130k]
    * Fixed a bug in my rounding function: negative values had not been rounded to the closest integer. This had resulted in higher relations modifiers for scoreboard rank and "first impressions" than intended. [advc.003]
    * Rewrote the formula for border tensions, increasing the importance of stolen and unworkable tiles. [advc.147]
    
    Tech value:
    * AI tech value for Animal Husbandry and Agriculture increased relative to Bronze Working and Iron Working. This was necessary because the AI is now (since v0.92) aware that health isn't important in the early game. Also had to water down the changes to chop value from K-Mod 1.46 a bit. [advc.036,k146]
    * Tech value of units: AI doesn't magically know whether it is geographically isolated until turn 30. [advc.131]
    * Reduced the tech value counted for buildings and trade routes in the very early game in order to make the AI less likely to research Sailing very early on. [advc.131]
    * Decreased the random value added to AI tech value (had too much impact in the early game). [advc.131]
    
    AI found value for river tiles tweaked; Tundra rivers had been overrated. [advc.031,advc.053]
    
    Delayed the appearance of Barbarian cities on small, unclaimed landmasses because it's difficult for the AI to conquer such cities. [advc.300]
    
    Non-AI changes:
    * Aligned the color coding of relations values in change advc.004q with the colors on the Glance tab. (Green for Pleased and Friendly, Red for Annoyed and Furious)
    * Sevopedia lists only improvements that can be built, and not e.g. City Ruins or "Land Worked". "Barbarian" no longer listed under leaders. [advc.004y]
    * Fixed a minor issue with city and tile culture conversion in my implementation of change dlph.23.

commit c6aea2ef244d56ab2f5318231077cf3116d08f26
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 1 23:51:46 2018 +0200

    Revised AI_foundValue
    (the function that determines where the AI settles)
    Still hardly tested
    [change id: advc.031 if none stated]
    
    Fixed a bug I introduced in v0.90; the bug had caused K-Mod code to be ignored that discourages settling on top of a resource. While looking for the bug, I've improved said K-Mod code a bit (hopefully). Also fixed a related issue introduced around that time: when a resource could not yet be improved, no bonus yields had been counted for that resource. Now bonus yields are counted if the tech requirement for trading the resource is currently researchable.
    
    Fixed a bug in K-Mod; code that was supposed to reduce found values in the proximity of other civs had had no effect. [advc.001]
    
    Per-tile utility values are now sorted in descending order and summed up with decreasing weights, meaning that more weight is given to tiles that are likely to be worked early in the city's life. (Previously, I had achieved a similar effect by taking per-tile values to the power of 1.25, but this would also encourage cities with uniformly good tiles, e.g. 20 river plains, when it might be better to split that area between several cities.)
    
    Some utility is counted for tiles in the radii of other cities, i.e. tiles that could be stolen from rival cities or shared with a friendly city.
    
    Rearranged code to make the function easier to read and to avoid some unnecessary or counterproductive computations. (It's still messy though, both conceptually and in terms of implementation.)
    
    Reconciled my own code for discouraging low-food sites and sites with too many bonus resources (advc.052) with BtS code serving a similar purpose.
    
    Reduced the AI aversion for sites with numerous bad tiles (e.g. Tundra) a bit further.
    
    In scenarios, the choice of the best city sites (function AI_updateCitySites) and the site that Settlers move to are now slightly randomized so that the AI doesn't necessarily pick the same spots for its first couple of cities in the same order every game. [advc.052]
    
    Unrelated to found value:
    The AI is now less likely to build Barracks before its first Settler. [advc.017]
    Animals can't appear on Desert and Snow tiles unless there is freshwater. [advc.300]

commit 7ea56f5bff2418f04df2c9f957dca7e47712e209
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jun 22 10:55:37 2018 +0200

    Some changes for scenarios:
    
    In scenarios, civs receive free tech from the game difficulty in addition to any free techs defined by the scenario. (E.g. AI civs start with Archery and Archers when playing the World18Civs scenario on Monarch difficulty, whereas, in BtS, they only start with Warriors.) [advc.051]
    
    The rule changes about peaks separating continents and ice separating oceans (advc.030) now apply to scenarios like they were supposed to. (But still don't apply to complex scenarios with preplaced cities like Earth1000AD.) [advc.051]
    
    Changes to AI found value:
    * On maps/ scenarios with densely placed resources, the AI avoids claiming too many resources with a single city. [advc.052]
    * "Greed" adjustment (based on AI personality and traits) removed because K-Mod's adjustment for Creative leaders does largely the same thing. [advc.031]
    * AI encouraged to settle in tiles that connect two large bodies of water. Only works if the water bodies are separated by land or ice though. [advc.031]

Change advc.122 was already converting culture in tiles surrounding the city, but I guess I forgot to also convert city culture. [dlph.23]

commit efd81e66a2a45883179fe685686deda828de4b09
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat May 5 00:21:17 2018 +0200

    Changes to Privateer
    [advc.033]
    Rules change: Civs in a vassal-master relationship can't use Privateers to pillage each other's improvements, blockade each other's cities nor to block tiles from being worked (CvUnit::canSiege). Combat still allowed.
    
    AI changes:
    * When selecting a city to plunder, attitude and the city owner's tech are taken into account. Depending on attitude and DeclareWarThemRefuseAttitudeThreshold, the AI doesn't use Privateers against ships and improvements.
    * Capitulated vassals don't train Privateers (unless they somehow don't have any better general-purpose ship).
    * Cities stop training Privateers once half of the world has entered the Industrial era.
    
    In Debug mode, Privateer ownership is revealed and Privateers are shown on the Military Advisor. [advc.007]

commit ce3cf805f64807a437e192e40e62dc5064c4f41c

    Further adjustments to the goody hut changes. In particular:
    - Increased peak turn from 200 to 225.
    - Huts can no longer grant progress toward Industrial and Modern tech.
    - Hostile units can have mixed types, e.g. 1 Archer and 1 Warrior.
    - Free units can start with up to two free promotions.
    - Spy can't get a free unit from a guarded hut (b/c it would land on top of the Barbarian unit guarding the hut).
    - AI units on "Reserve" enter a Tribal Village if one happens to be near them. This can matter when the AI founds a colony on an unexplored landmass.
    [advc.314]

    * (A few comments added about minor known issues.)
    
    (Commented out in the code because it seems like a needless complication on second thought and dubious historically: When a city is clearly about to be conquered, the AI is willing to cede that city in a peace deal.)  [advc.122]

commit 2989cda6e0a97c60bd15d38a45913209af8c701e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Feb 22 16:00:07 2018 +0100

    Toward v0.92 (no DLL committed):
    
    Improvements to the PerfectMongoose (PM) map script:
    * The break-Pangaea code is now properly disabled when playing without the Old World Starts option. It was supposed to work this way since v0.89.
    * Further reduced the number and size of meteors used for breaking Pangaea (when playing with Old World Starts).
    * Smoothed the impact of meteors on elevation levels; fewer Peaks along coasts this way and more Peaks elsewhere.
    * Increased the size of the Old World a bit. Continents that are too small for civs to start on are now always counted as part of the New World.
    * Let PM assign starting locations even when playing without Old World Starts. Previously, I had used the standard assignment algorithm from the DLL instead.
    * Made the PM assignment of starting locations prioritize distance between starting locations more.
    * Fur no longer appears on high elevations in low latitudes.
    
    Tidied up some changes from the last few commits; also some bugfixes.
    
    Usability improvements for AI resource trades:
    * When an AI civ both buys resources from and sells resources to another AI civ, the AI tries to cancel those deals and replace them with resource-for-resource trades. This should make the AI trades easier to read on the Foreign Advisor. [advc.036]
    * In one-for-one resource trades, the AI is willing to give human players a small discount in order to avoid asking for 1 gold per turn in addition. [advc.036]
    * AI willingness to cancel resource deals due to uneven trade values now based on the age of the deal. [advc.133]
    
    Merged a bugfix by EmperorFool: Accessing the Civilopedia from the main menu (without having started or loaded a game first) no longer causes Sevopedia to become permanently disabled. [advc.004y]
    
    Went through the post-K-Mod BUG commit history and merged another bug fix: The strategy overlay (dot map) no longer disappears after loading a savegame.
    
    Replays record the first discovery of each tech. Can alternatively (XML switch) report when a civ enters a new era. Replay messages about founded cities are shown in the city owner's text color. [advc.106]
    
    Decreased the value assigned by the City AI to Moai Statues and Globe Theater in the capital. [advc.131]
    
    Bug fixed in advc.004b (projected expenses shown on city found button): Had not been taking into account colony maintenance in other cities.
    
    Barbarians are no longer able to train Paratroopers. [advc.307]
    
    PublicMaps folder changed to "PrivateMaps" based on TC01's recommendation here:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/private-and-public-maps.355021/

commit ed1826faf199f4a18442c9196f181a46797e79c1
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Feb 18 11:27:13 2018 +0100

    Toward v0.92 (no DLL committed):
    Adjustments to advc.099b (tile culture decay in city radii):
    * Tiles contested between more than two civs are now handled sensibly. Removed the term "exclusive radius" from the manual and some variable names because it's misleading: decay can also apply to a tile within the radius of more than one city.
    * Tiles owned by Barbarians and city tiles exempted from decay beyond the 1% that applies to all tiles.
    * Decay rate reduced a little.
    
    Two bugs fixed in k146 (tech evaluation): illegal tech selected; infinite loop.
    Made the AI less interested in beelining toward powerful techs (DepthRate reduced from 0.8 to 0.6). [k146]
    
    UWAI:
    * Improved the performance of distance measurements. This could speed up AI turns in the late game by some 5%.
    * Improved the simulation of wars between civs spread across multiple landmasses. That said, there's still hardly any AI warfare on Archipelago before the Industrial era. Conquering small islands is just rarely worth the effort because the tactical AI needs a lot of units to pull it off (and then faces problems with stranded units).
    * Fixed an issue with war utility from "bellicosity" counting war successes of allies.
    Plus some misc. tweaks, mostly for performance.
    
    UI (minor):
    * Fixed some bugs that I had introduced in v0.90 when refactoring CvGameTextMgr.cpp. Help text for buildings hadn't been shown in Civilopedia when viewing it from the main menu, and some info was missing (e.g. the project names in the help text for the projects list).
    * Added unit costs to the help text for the units list (were missing in BtS).
    The number of buildings required for national wonders is now computed assuming Standard world size when accessing Civilopedia from the main menu (instead of Duel size). [advc.004y]
    * Get to see all foreign units in Military Advisor when in Debug mode. (Wish I had done that long ago. And how easy it was!) Can no longer switch some of the Advisor screens to the Barbarian perspective when in Debug mode. [advc.007]

commit ad5faf8aa2740b991c49d8f35e14769d190a4c71
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Feb 15 17:58:01 2018 +0100

    Test version incl. DLL and manual; needs some more work.
    
    Game rules changes:
    * When a tile is within the workable radius of a city, the tile culture of all civs that don't have a city nearby decays by 3.5% to 6% each turn. (A 1% decay rate on all tiles had already been implemented in v0.80.) This change replaces advc.035 (cities own all tiles in their exclusive radius), which is now disabled. [advc.099b]
    * Hereditary Rule nerfed: Grants 1 happiness per every 2 military units and +25% happiness from resources. [advc.912c]
    
    Bugfixes (all in AdvCiv code):
    * In advc.300 (AI code for guarding high-yield tiles against barbarians): Crash to desktop was possible on maps without world-wrap.
    * In advc.210a: Might've caused a crash (array read at position -1) when loading a savegame from within a game with a higher number of civs ever alive than in the savegame.
    * In advc.106c: The BUG alert about gold trades (disabled by default) had been unusable (Python exception) since v0.80.
    * In advc.120d: Coloring of espionage mission costs. I thought I had fixed this in v0.91, but it still didn't work correctly.
    * In advc.001f: Messages about razed cities hadn't been sent.
    * Amended a bugfix in the AI code for trade proposals (advc.001). My earlier fix had sometimes led the AI to overcharge humans.
    * Some UWAI code to discourage early dogpile wars had had no effect; now enabled.
    * The v0.91 manual had lots of broken links; must've happened when exporting to PDF. The links in the v0.91b manual seem fine. The source of the manual (ODT format) is now on git too.
    
    AI changes:
    * Overhaul of AI resource trades: If the AI doesn't need the happiness or health from a resource, it refuses to import that type of resource and is willing to export all of its own resources of that type. And several related AI changes; see change id 036 in the manual.
    * Adjusted advc.149 ("years you supplied us with resources") to change 036. Should be a bit easier to get a relations bonus than in v0.91. Vassal tribute no longer counts.
    * The AI can demand gold per turn as tribute. [advc.104m]
    * Added can-trade checks before AI demands for maps and cash. These had been missing in BtS and may have led to fewer tribute demands than had been intended. [advc.001]
    * When considering to cancel a resource trade, the AI checks all trade-denial conditions. Will e.g. cancel a trade based on attitude or when the other side has acquired an imported resource on the map. [advc.133]
    * Greater AI reluctance to cancel resource deals that no longer look fair in terms of trade value. When an AI-AI resource deal is canceled, the two AI civs immediately try to renegotiate. [advc.133]
    * Reduced the discount on resource trades from voluntary vassals (67% instead of 50%); and voluntary vassals refuse to trade resource that they badly need themselves. [advc.037]
    * Resource trades now contribute to the diplo penalty for trading with an enemy, although the contribution is pretty small. [advc.130p]
    * Whether the AI counts tech-received memory ("We fear you're becoming too advanced") now depends on the recipient's era, not (as in K-Mod) on the game era, and tech-received memory for "You shared your discoveries" is counted under the same conditions; i.e. techs that are 2 eras behind the recipient's era don't count, and techs that the recipient had already almost discovered by itself (2/3 progress) don't count either.
    Such insignificant trades are now unaffected by the normal 1-turn tech brokering delay and by the no-tech-brokering option. I.e. trading a tech to an AI civ that is almost through researching that tech will not prevent the AI civ from trading with the tech when "no tech brokering" is enabled. [advc.550e]
    * When choosing the gold target for its treasury, the AI takes the potential for tech trades and war trades into account. An AI civ may try to buy the tech that it is currently researching from another AI civ. To facilitate tech purchases from humans, the AI is willing to pay more gold to humans when the AI gets close to discovering a tech. [advc.550f]
    * Reduced the frequency of unattractive AI-to-human tech trade proposals a bit. [advc.550b]
    * Revised the computation of the AI's civics and religion trade value; specifically, the formula that accounts for anarchy. [advc.132]
    * The AI refuses to trade for the human map when it's worth less than 5 gold. [advc.136b]
    * Tiles that the AI steals from a neighbor through culture, but is unable to work because they're too far away, add to the diplo penalty for border tensions. [advc.147]
    * AI a bit more reluctant to settle near the human capital in a One-City Challenge. [advc.031]
    * In human-AI teams (team game or Permanent Alliance), the AI no longer accepts all trades proposed by the human; only accepts if the trade is at least somewhat even. Can reject gift requests. Human can't offer to switch civics or religion (jdog's unofficial patch allowed this, probably by accident). [advc.155]
    
    UWAI changes:
    * If UWAI is enabled, the AI makes almost all of its cash and gold-per-turn available when negotiating peace. (That said, UWAI has its own boundaries on reparations.) [advc.104w]
    * Reduced UWAI's drive to declare war when the BtS no-war probability would be 100% due to attitude. This makes the AI hesitate longer before turning on a friend, and gives it a stronger preference for picking a different target instead.
    * Slightly reduced the utility assigned by UWAI to resolving border disputes.
    * Increased the willingness of the AI to prepare for a naval war in situations when the AI has very few ships.
    * Slightly tightened the conditions for being hired for war against a remote target. [advc.104o]
    * Fixed some more issues with team games: The AI ...
    - realizes that a team-on-team war is not a dogpile war and doesn't subtract utility for "fair play" reasons.
    - is not worried about a "war on friend" penalty from members of the attacked team (there is no such penalty).
    - is generally less worried about diplomatic ill will in team games.
    - doesn't count utility for assisting a team member. (That's already covered by adding up the war utility of all team members in the end.)
    - increases the war utility counted for conquered cities a bit when it's a team-on-team war in order to increase AI aggressiveness.
    - no longer tries to predict capitulations of teams with more than one surviving member.
    
    UI changes:
    * Peace terms are announced to third parties. [advc.039]
    * Reactivated the top civs popup ("Pliny the Elder has completed his greatest work ..."), but it only appears until the player has met more than half of the other civs. "Wealthiest" is now based on GNP and "most advanced" on the total cost of known techs. And some minor adjustments to the timing of the popup. [advc.038]
    * Religion spread in foreign cities is only announced to the player if the new religion differs from the city owner's state religion, or when the player owns the religion's holy city. [advc.106e]
    * The trade table no longer shows resources that the other side already has access to ("Surely, you must be joking" in BtS). [advc.004]
    * Added a Civ4lert about third-party resource trades. Disabled by default. [advc.210d]
    * Units are no longer shown on the minimap. More opaque minimap colors on land tiles. Also increased opacity on the Military Advisor map. [advc.002a]
    * Reduced the vertical space between Minimap buttons and Advanced Scoreboard (the BUG scoreboard, which is enabled by default). [advc.106d]
    * In team games, team membership is color-coded on the scoreboard. [advc.155]
    * In messages about GP birth, only the GP name is shown in yellow. This should make the messages easier to distinguish from BUG gold trade alerts. [advc.106]
    * When negotiating a peace treaty, the trade screen says "10 turns" again. v0.91 had accidentally changed it to "0 turns". [advc.004w]
    * Help text on national wonders indicates the number of national wonders that the city can still build. Show "0 left" in red on wonders that are already in construction in another city. [advc.004w]
    * Put the "AD" before the year number in all game text. [advc.002k]
    * In a One City Challenge, the game difficulty is treated as 3 levels higher when computing the victory score. [advc.250]
    * Loading screen hint added about vassal tribute deals: the first demand is always accepted. [advc.008d]
    * Added German translations of all my changes to Civilopedia. [advc.008, advc.005e]
    * Added Google translations in the Romance languages for the AdvCiv alerts (revolt, war trade). [advc.210ab]

    v0.90b:

    * When choose-production popups are canceled because of anarchy, the city now remembers the most recently finished order and displays it when the popup is relaunched. Also, the popup didn't reliably reappear in the previous version. [advc.004x]
    * A tweak to the v0.90 change to "appreciate ... you supplied us with resources": When deciding whether to increment its turn counter for resource trade, the AI takes into account how many resources the giving side has available for trade.     * A tweak to change 045, which hides 3D models of rival buildings: When any unit of the player is inside the rival city tile, all buildings are shown. Previously, there had to be a Spy unit ready to investigate the city.
    * Small bug in 001c fixed; GP birth probabilities hadn't summed up to 100.

commit d6ec40eead25f18975f1bafe07e04f8f3fdb43fa
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Nov 13 02:16:04 2017 +0100

    v0.90:
    * When playing with "Minimize Pop-Ups", redundant and outdated choose-tech, change-civics and change-religion popups are killed. [advc.004x]
    * Settings tab (Victory screen) shows the initial number of civs. [advc.004]

    * Fixed a bug in change 004m that had caused the field-of-view size to shift on each return to the main menu (i.e. also on each Quick Load due to change 003d).
    * The AI puts exploring Galleys and Work Boats to different tasks once it has access to Caravels. This ensures that the AI actual trains Caravels for exploration rather than assuming that it already has enough explorers. [advc.017b]
    * AI no longer asks the player for help, tribute or an embargo when war against the player is already imminent. [advc.104m]
    * Made Willem less willing to attack when Pleased by increasing his no-war probability. Had been 80%, which ties with e.g. Alexander and Montezuma; now 90% like most other leaders who declare war when Pleased. Earlier versions had already tweaked Willem's victory weights and MaxWarRand in order to make him less of a warmonger. [advc.005a]
    * Crash fixed when loading a non-R&F game from within a R&F game after inspecting a city. [advc.706]
    
    UWAI changes:
    * When counting the total trade assets that a player is able pay in order to hire the AI for war, cities are now ignored because the AI doesn't accept cities as payment for war.
    * Some fair-play clauses added that make the AI reluctant to attack human players in the early game when they have already lost cities, and that discourage ganging up on a single weak target.
    * When considering which buildings could be constructed in cities instead of military build-up, religious buildings are counted only under certain conditions. Civs with many religions had previously overestimated the opportunity cost of war a bit.
    
    And some very minor misc. tweaks.

commit 71fa4eef1a22df6b910bb41a5dc68d3ca9c3586d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Nov 5 11:26:30 2017 +0100

    v0.90rc (release candidate in need of more testing):
    Many further tweaks to AI found value [advc.031,advc.040], in particular:
    * AI less interested in city sites with resources that can't yet be worked, especially strategic resources like Oil when the AI already owns an unimproved copy.
    * Decreased the bonus value assigned by the AI to early strategic resources and increased the value for late ones like Oil and Uranium (once they can be worked and units require them). [advc.031]
    * Fixed a bug that had led the K-Mod AI to found early cities in the jungle.
    
    Player color palette revised: Shifted most colors a little bit to make them easier to distinguish or less painful to look at. See comparison in manual under id 002i.
    
    Finished change 030 (ice-locked sea areas; much more work than I had expected), and made various amendments to changes in the previous two commits, in particular:
    * Textures: Restored BtS Snow texture because the Blue Marble texture looks too similar to my Tundra texture. Farms more saturated. Roads lighter, more brown. [advc.002h]
    * Lighthouse and Levee shown as 3D models in rival cities because their presence can be inferred from the tile yield change. [advc.045]
    
    Misc. changes:
    * Only revealed cities are considered for the list of high-culture cities on the Victory screen. (Unrevealed cities had already been excluded from the Top 5 cities on the Statistics screen since v0.80.) [advc.001d]
    * Privateers can no longer plunder gold across land. BBAI had already fixed this for blockaded plots, but not for plunder. [advc.033]
    * AI a little bit more willing to attack cities without (full) prior bombardment. [advc.114c]
    * Improved the way that UWAI handles situations in which the best military unit that a civ could train isn't supposed to be known to the AI.
    * UWAI no longer overcounts angry citizens when in disorder.
    * Efficiency and accuracy of UWAI inter-city distance measurements improved.
    * Some code added to properly initialize the AI in scenarios. (E.g. the initial citizen assignment was messed up for some reason in Earth1000AD.) [advc.104u]
    * Barbarian Galleys no longer try to drop units on territory protected by the Great Wall. [advc.306]
    
    Plus some minor tweaks not worth spelling out. [advc.045,115b,115d,104o,300,137,148,cdtw]

commit b50e4a9a5a243f4f582213df1b07bae12dfb142a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Nov 3 11:29:12 2017 +0100

    Not a stable version yet; current DLL and manual not included; change 030 (Ice can separate water areas) work in progress; only pushing this for backup purposes.
    
    AI changes, most of them in the UWAI mod component:
    * When a civ brings in a war ally against the AI, the attacked AI refuses to talk with both war enemies for (on average) 12.5 turns. Previously, the attacked AI had only refused to talk to the hired civ. [advc.130i]
    * When the AI is in a war and thinks that joining that war would have a very low war utility (a high negative value) for a human civ, then the AI does not ask the human civ to join the war. It may instead ask for a trade embargo. [advc.130m]
    * During the midgame, UWAI takes into account commerce rates when deciding which civs are the likeliest to win the game. Previously, only score was considered (fair enough in the early game) and progress toward victory conditions (important in the endgame). Also fixed a bug that had caused scores to be mixed up.
    * Made UWAI a bit quicker to start war preparations when war utility is positive.
    * Reduced the flat cost for ravages of war and war-time economy that is subtracted from AI war utility.
    * No war utility for becoming the only likely winner if this means declaring war on a liked civ (one that the BtS AI would never declare war on).
    * When all trade items of the (human) player aren't enough to convince the AI to declare war on a third party, the AI now refuses to even discuss that war ("too much on our hands", "nothing to gain" or "fear their might"). This reduces the number of messages generated by the war-trades alert. As before, the AI also refuses to discuss a joint war when the utility value of that war is below a constant threshold (of -32).
    * Made the AI a bit more willing to build the Manhattan Project, especially in large games. [advc.650]
    * Fixed a likely bug in the K-Mod found value code that had caused the AI to overrate additional copies of strategic resources. Tweaked AI found values to prevent the AI from settling awful coastal sites, and to make the AI willing to accept sites with lots of bad tiles but some really good ones. [advc.031]
    * AI recognizes water cordoned off by ice as a separate water area and takes this into account when deciding whether to build ships. Rarely relevant on most map scripts, but Pangaea and Archipelago tend to have ice-locked bodies of water. (I had already made a similar change for land enclosed by peaks in v0.87.) [advc.030]
    * Stages of the AI diplo victory strategy tweaked; had been too quick to aim for an Apostolic Palace victory. [advc.115b]
    * Diplo from rank further tweaked: AI civs at stage 3 or 4 of a victory strategy assign a "getting ahead of us" penalty only to civs at victory stage 4. [advc.130c]
    * Minor bug fixed in change 130: Trade between capitulated vassal and master can no longer lead to an enemy-trade diplo penalty.
    * Adopted some AI tweaks from Dave_uk's LoR SDK ModMod. Change id: cdtw
    
    UI changes:
    * Capitulated vassals removed from the "Glance" tab of the Foreign Advisor screen. [advc.130v]
    * Help text on Foreign Advisor screen says "vassal (voluntary)" rather than just "vassal" when a vassal has not capitulated. (An earlier change had already added "vassal (capitulated)".) [advc.130v]
    * Fixed an issue with change 120c (Espionage slider only shown when above 0). The UI now gets properly updated.
    * Terrain textures added: BML.fpk (for "Blue Marble Light"); based on Kai Fiebach's Blue Marble. Drifting clouds in Globe View disabled. [advc.002h]
    * Main menu (the one that appears right after launching BtS): Items that don't work ("BtS Content", "Check for Updates") or that aren't recommendable ("Play Now!", "Play Scenario") shown in gray. [advc.002g]
    * Default field of view value reduced (camera angle more top-down). This has no effect of field if view is set through the BUG slider. [advc.004m]
    * From Rise of Mankind: Only wonders and defensive buildings are shown in rival cities on the main interface. [advc.045]
    * Restricted the information provided by the Espionage screen: Cost for Sabotage Production and Sabotage Building no longer shown. Instead, all sabotage missions except Sabotage Project appear as a single line "Sabotage" with a question mark in the cost column. For the Steal missions the amount of gold/ cheapest tech are shown. (That's what the costs of these missions are based on.) [advc.120d]
    (I've accidentally used id 120d twice. The earlier 120d is now 120e.)
    
    * Non-AI/UI changes: Fixed a bug that (I think) had caused Deity difficulty to be treated as King difficulty as far as research modifiers are concerned, and that, since the removal of King difficulty, had crashed Deity games. [advc.250a]

commit b6dd1b55da0412a72086e8fb245f920f9060b00f
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Oct 19 22:47:15 2017 +0200

    Towards v0.90 (hardly tested yet):
    * Penalty on human-AI relations from difficulty replaced with a bonus on AI-AI relations. Attitude thresholds changed accordingly: +4 for Pleased, Annoyed at -2 or worse, Furious at -8. Friendly remains at +10, meaning that it actually becomes "1 easier" to reach. Friendly attitude required for diplo victory vote (BtS: +8 relations suffice). [advc.148]
    * AI diplo bonus from resource trade now takes longer to attain/increase when the recipient already has many resources. Also fixed a sign error in v0.80 that had caused the trade counter (on which the diplo bonus is based) to further increase - instead of decrease - when a resource trade stopped. [advc.149]
    * The speed at which the Open Borders counter of the AI increases is now based on the trade routes and geographical distance between the cities of the two sides. (This counter determines the "Open Borders have brought us together" bonus.) [advc.130i]
    * All AI diplo counters (e.g. Open Borders, resource trade) decrease by 1.7% per turn when they're not increased. Previously, these counters were decreased by 1 instead. [advc.130k]
    * Reduced the AI-AI diplo modifier from warmonger respect to 75% and the modifier from peace weight to 45%. (In previous versions, the peace weight bonus had been halved and rounded up instead.) The sum of the two modifiers (rounded to nearest) now ranges from -3 to +3. [advc.130b]
    * Capitulated vassals vote for the same candidate as their master in diplo votes. Had previously only voted for the master when the master was a candidate. [advc.130v]
    * Tweaked change 147 (fewer tiles counted for the border-tensions diplo penalty).
    * Made the AI quicker to propose Open Borders to other AI civs once both sides are willing to sign. (Inspired by Civ 4 Reimagined.) [advc.124]
    * No diplo bonus from rank ("you're hardly a threat") when the low-ranked civ is at stage 3 or 4 of an AI victory strategy. [advc.130c]
    * AI attitude cache gets updated when the ranks on the scoreboard are updated. (AI attitude not always being up-to-date is an issue inherited from the BBAI mod.) [advc.001]
    * Victoria and Bismarck forget tribute demands like everyone else after 30 turns on average. I had somehow missed these two when making change 130r (decay of all AI diplo memory).
    * Increased the utility assigned by UWAI for getting closer to a military victory. When a war enemy is expected to capitulate, its remaining cities and population are now factored into the utility from getting closer to a Domination victory (previously, capitulations had only been considered for Conquest and Diplo victory).
    * Impact of affection on war utility reduced to 87% of the previous versions. This makes it a bit easier for peaceable leaders like Saladin to declare war despite Pleased attitude, though it still only happens in exceptional circumstances. Also makes the AI more willing to start wars overall. (Even at Cautious, many leaders have some affection for their war targets.) Can easily undo this by changing UWAI_WEIGHT_AFFECTION in AI_Variables_GlobalDefines.xml.
    * Tweaked AI stack sizes because I had noticed that Medieval and Renaissance stacks of non-militaristic AI leaders were often too small to conquer other AI cities. [advc.104p]
    * Improved change 115. Previously, the AI did not pursue a Space victory when its cities had way too little production, but would still build the Apollo Project. Now doesn't build Apollo either.
    * Cities can receive military happiness (fear for safety, Hereditary Rule) only from units of the same team or a vassal or master. [advc.001o]
    * King difficulty setting (introduced in v0.80) removed. See advc.250a in the manual about how to re-enable it.
    * Got rid of some unhelpful help text on the city screen, especially in the list of completed buildings. [advc.004w, advc.004a]
    * More hills on PerfectMongoose maps. There had been about as many as on Fractal maps, but it seems that more are needed because PerfectMongoose tends to place them in clusters. [advc.021b]
    * Increased the initial camera distance a little bit further. [advc.004m]
    * Change 130z (AI becomes unwilling to sign Open Borders at the end of a war) removed because, since v0.89, change 130r accomplishes the same thing (and more elegantly).

    v0.89:
    * Rise & Fall:
    ** Scoring delay further reduced. 50% into the second chapter (no change), but with each chapter, the delay decreases a little. The penultimate chapter is scored 25% into the final chapter.
    ** Score premium from victory reduced: Base value ("P") reduced from 300 to 150. Score from time remaining equal to the percentage of time remaining (instead of 1.5 times the percentage). Formula for normalized score adjusted accordingly.
    ** Year of the end turn added to Score tab; e.g. "Turn 0 to 64 (1440 BC)".
    ** Minor correction to the info displayed on the Score tab when play continues after victory.
    
    * Made the AI a bit more willing to commit to stages 3 and 4 of the domination victory strategy in large games. [advc.115]
    * Use stricter requirements for stage 4 of the culture victory strategy, but only in UWAI and R&F, when the victory stage is computed for gauging how close a civ is to (any) victory condition.
    * The AI refuses to sign a vassal agreement when it has at least one defensive pact and isn't in any war. [advc.112]
    * Reduced AI trade value for cities that are being evacuated: When the AI thinks that a city is about to be conquered, it becomes more willing to trade that city away, and less willing to pay for it. [advc.139]
    * Placed a limit on the number of lost tiles that can be counted per city when computing the diplo penalty from border tensions. Don't want a single city choked by foreign culture to result in a high diplo penalty for the owner of that foreign culture. [advc.147]
    * Another tweak to change 130h: When deciding whether to assign a war-on-friend diplo penalty, the AI checks if that friend has recently attacked another friend. Previously, only the at-war status between the friends was checked, and not which side attacked and when.
    * No longer receive a Declare War popup when moving into a tile where there are both hostile units and units of a third party. karadoc had already disabled this popup in most situations, but it seems that he missed this one. [advc.001]
    * Minor change to text on scoreboard: "Ctrl for trade table" and "Alt to declare war" on a single line. [advc.004v]
    * Loading screen hint added about change 003d (faster loading through Alt+Tab).
    * Disabled some help text shown in debug mode. [advc.007]

commit beb230a3bafeecd05c7efba87b45b6bd1615e121
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Oct 9 15:52:18 2017 +0200

    More additions to v0.89rc:
    * Shift+F8 (Quick Load) briefly exits to main menu before loading the savegame. This is much faster than loading directly (though maybe not on all systems).
    When exiting to the main menu, the game no longer forgets whether resource bubbles had been enabled. [advc.003d,advc.004m]
    * In-game main menu renamed from "Main Menu" to "Game Menu" in help text. (The true "Main Menu" is where you go via "Exit to Main Menu".) [advc.004g]
    
    * Improvements to AI willingness to talk in some specific situations:
    ** Refuse-to-talk (RTT) duration from embargoes reduced from 30 turns on average to 25. RTT duration after a declaration of war at the request of another civ reduced to 12.5 turns on average (previously 15 turns). [advc.130f]
    ** Refusal to talk after an embargo and refusal to sign a treaty after cancelation no longer depend on AI attitude. (Previously, as a side-effect of change 130j, the refusal durations were shortened when the other side was Annoyed or Furious and prolonged when Friendly.)
    ** Memory about recently canceled deals can decay only partially while at war. This means that the AI is never willing to sign Open Borders right after a war ends. [advc.130r]
    ** When a DoW is triggered through a defensive pact (DP), the AI refuses to talk for 12.5 turns on average. In previous versions, unless UWAI was disabled, there was nothing to prevent one of the DP allies from making peace after a couple of turns. Also, the RTT durations from DP and sponsored war no longer stack with the RTT duration from trade embargoes. [advc.104i]
    
    * No more war-on-friend penalties for attacking a capitulated vassal (only for attacking the master). [advc.130h]
    * Upon becoming a vassal, AI civs forget any "arrogant" demands.  (Because I don't want the diplomatic protection from accepting a demand to extend from the vassal to the master.) [advc.130o]
    * When a peace treaty gets signed between two civs that already have a peace treaty, the turns-to-cancel on the existing treaty are reset to 10. (In BtS, the signing of the second treaty has no effect.) [advc.032]
    * Replaced several instances of "pass" in my v0.89rc Python code with "return" after discovering that "pass" does not cause a function to return. My misconception had led to some unnecessary computations, mostly in Civ4lerts, and a couple of changes to PerfectMongoose had had no effect.
    
    * Rise & Fall:
    ** Civs close to a victory condition are considered to be ranked higher than those not close to any victory. This is relevant for the computation of the Rise score (which is based on ranks). I've changed this because the ranking on the leader board is not a good measure of a civ's standing during the endgame. I'm using the BBAI victory stages to determine whether a civ is close (stage 3) or very close (stage 4) to victory. The dialog for civ selection now shows when a civ is close to victory.
    ** Bug fixed that had exempted vassals of previously played civs from AI trade restrictions.
    ** Bug fixed that had prevented diplomacy between AI civs on the first turn of a chapter.
    ** Auto Play countdown corrected; had been one turn ahead.
    ** In v0.89rc, the AI already got to make some decisions on the final turn of a chapter (after the player presses "End Turn"). Now the final turn is entirely under human control.
    ** Civ4lerts are no longer displayed on the first turn of a chapter.
    ** Redundant minimized tech choice popups no longer appear on the first turn of a chapter.
    
    * Reduced display duration of Civ4lerts from long to normal. Had already meant to do this in v0.80, but missed one half of the alerts. [advc.106c]
    * The message about an unclaimed resource revealed by a new tech is now based on the revealed owner (which can differ from the actual owner) of the resource tile. [advc.004r]
    * Changed a few loading screen hints. [advc.008c,advc.008d]

Previously, the AI would then become willing to talk, but reject all proposals for peace. Also, the AI now agrees to fewer reparations after a while if the human doesn't have enough to give.

    * "Show Friendly Moves" no longer shows patrolling AI Galleys (previously shown b/c Galleys could, principally, carry attackers). And gave AI patrols a slight tendency to avoid tiles with a foreign owner. [advc.102]
    * Amendment to the change in v0.86 that lets the AI refuse to declare war on targets that are farther away than its current war enemies: now takes land connection into account (only air distance considered in v0.86). [advc.104o, advc.210a]
    * Fixed a UWAI issue that had made the AI reluctant to start or continue war when the target had far fewer cities. [advc.104o]
    * Fixed a UWAI crash upon the creation of an independent colony by the AI. [advc.104r]
    * Tweaked the army, navy and home guard portions in the UWAI armament forecast, and partially implemented an estimate for enemy navy power (until that's done, UWAI continues to magically know the enemy navy power).
    * Several changes that let the AI build fewer ships (especially before Renaissance):
    ** Potential bug fixed in BBAI code that may have lead to large AI fleets when only a "minimal attack force" had been intended. [advc.017b]
    ** AI builds fewer escort ships when the enemy is expected to have a small navy. [advc.017]
    ** Added a few rules that allow AI ships to change between tasks, e.g. from attacker to explorer for (upgraded) Caravels. [advc.017]
    * Made the AI willing to send a Settler to an only partially explored  (potential) city site when that site is on the coast of an unclaimed continent. I.e. doesn't have to explore inland first. [advc.040]
    * Other minor tweaks to AI found values. [advc.031]
    * AI less alert about a potential attack when not on the same continent. [advc.022]
    * Made capitulated vassals a bit more reluctant to found cities (considering that the master will have to pay some maintenance for the new city too). [advc.130v]
    * Minor tweaks to AI razing: less inclined to raze barbarian cities on other continents; don't always raze when thwarting a culture victory. [advc.300, advc.116]
    * Slightly increased AI target stack size for naval assaults. [advc.104p]
    * Minor personality change to Willem: Shifted victory weight a bit from Conquest to Culture and slightly lowered his affinity for dogpile wars. v0.80 had already reduced his readiness to start "total" wars. [advc.005a]
    * No rank hate ("getting ahead of us") when the score ratio is greater than 150%. This should eliminate rank hate in cases when two civs are ranked close to each other, but one has far higher score than the other. Generally, rank hate shouldn't apply when a lead is uncatchable. [advc.130c]
    * Fixed a rare BtS bug that had allowed the AI to offer a Defensive Pact right after getting attacked by a third party. [advc.001e]
    * If another civ razes a revealed but not presently visible city of a third party, borders are now properly updated in the fog of war. [advc.001f]
    * "You have discovered ..." audio played in multiplayer again (K-Mod had been playing tech quotes instead). [advc.201]
    * Documentation files from BBAI 1.01 added. (K-Mod is based on BBAI but hadn't kept those files around.) [advc.009]
    * (Some comments added after another unsuccessful attempt to work around the peace-offer bug in the EXE.) [advc.134a]

commit 4c92031c6a1f44a2466e1343864d4f1181a2ebd9
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jun 25 18:35:19 2017 +0200

    v0.86:
    * Human civs get a 5% bonus vs. barbarians on Monarch, Emperor and Immortal (now the same as on Prince). (change 313)
    * The "Show ... Moves" options no longer show when a unit moves through a visible tile but starts and ends the turn in invisible tiles. (v0.85 had started to show such moves, but couldn't "catch" the moving unit, showing only the empty traversed tile, which was confusing.)
    * Minor bug fixed in change 004r. Messages about revealed resources had sometimes been giving away the names of unrevealed cities.
    * Can no longer spread religions and corporations during disorder. (change 099d)
    * Impact of religion on revolt probability reduced. (change 099c)
    * When a master asks its capitulated vassal to stop trading with a rival, that embargo no longer cancels trades between the master and the rival, and the rival doesn't stop talking to the master. This an exception to change 130f. The only negative consequence for the master is the "you negotiated a trade embargo" diplo penalty - as in BtS. Unlike in BtS, capitulated vassals agree to such embargoes without compensation.
    * Capitulated vassals again (as in v0.84) share their master's attitude toward rivals, but are at best Cautious. Always Cautious regardless of master attitude (v0.85) meant that vassals would often have Open Borders with their master's worst enemies - bad idea. (change 130v)
    * AI raze evaluation adjusted; AI had been too willing to raze when in financial trouble. (change 116)
    * Impact of rank-based diplo reduced in the early game: No "You're getting ahead of us" penalty when the difference in score is less than 25 points. (change 130c)
    It's still too fickle; should really be based on score entirely and not on rank.
    * UWAI no longer plans war while there is a peace treaty resulting from received tribute. Once the peace treaty ends, the AI remains reluctant to plan war for (on average) 10 turns. More specifically, the (human) civ that payed tribute is treated as if the AI attitude was Pleased. These changes should make a DoW shortly after receiving tribute unlikely. (change 130o)
    * Fixed a bug in UWAI that had caused success from past wars to be ignored. Should now work and (to an extent) discourage repeated unsuccessful wars against the same target.
    * Reduced AI tendency to dogpile on humans that appear to be on the ropes, and reduced AI tendency for dogpile wars a bit overall.
    * Reduced the time that arrogant demands are remembered from 80 to 30. Should've been 30 since v0.80, and that's what the manual said too. (change 130r/130o)
    * AI now charges at least as much for starting a war as for stopping trade. In the previous (UWAI) versions, war was sometimes cheaper than an embargo.
    Embargo now a bit cheaper if Pleased or Friendly with the civ that asks for it.
    (change 130f/104o)
    * Increased the lower bound for the trade value that the AI assigns to starting a war at the request of another civ. In the previous versions, the AI was sometimes willing to start wars for very little compensation when already in a war and losing badly.
    * Trade value for starting a war now also based on the utility of war against the sponsor. This is to account for the peace treaty between the hired civ and the sponsor (change 146).
    * The AI can no longer be hired for war against a target that is farther away than a current war enemy, unless the new enemy is already at war with the human player. This should reduce the number of messages generated by the "War Trades" alert (change 210a).
    * Two related changes: In BtS peace negotiations, it's principally possible to hire the AI for war or to propose an embargo. However, the AI practically always refuses on account of attitude, which makes it pointless to show these items on the trade screen. So, I'm removing war trades from the trade screen when negotiating peace, but I'm keeping the embargoes, and the AI agrees to them regardless of attitude. Attitude still factors into the trade value that the AI assigns to an embargo. (changes 100 and 130f)
    * Disabled change dlph.10 (civ forced to abandon its state religion when no longer controlling a city with that religion). Actually, it never even worked because I had forgotten to merge a line from DarkLunaPhantom's mod.

commit c01c07e94be3b86fa524a1cb14cff918d0996ae3
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Jun 9 02:26:34 2017 +0200

    v0.85: Early ships (further) buffed; "show moves" options improved; changes to "begging for peace"; power thresholds for capitulation adjusted; other AI improvements
    
    * Trireme now base strength 3, but no bonus vs. Galley. +1 speed for Caravel. -5 cost for Galley and Trireme. See change 905 in manual.
    * The air unit cap (4 per city) no longer prevents air units from upgrading. (Fixes a bug in change 001b.)
    * Air units and post-Medieval siege units now ignore defensive buildings entirely, not just the bombardment reduction effect; see change 004c in the manual.
    * Tweaked revolt probability (change 101):
    Slightly reduced if owner has no state religion (but not as much as with a state religion that is present in the city).
    Reduced in cities that have a high population when conquered; e.g. a size-10 Renaissance city had been too difficult to pacify in the previous version.
    * "Show friendly moves" now shows moving ships only if (a) it's a cargo ship; or (b) the ship enters or leaves sight; or (c) the ship moves inside the player's borders. (change 102)
    * The "Show moves" options now also show when a unit moves out of sight. (BtS showed only moves ending on visible tiles.)
    * AI now considers war utility against the player when deciding whether to grant a gift request. AI memory about gift requests doesn't decay while there is a peace treaty. I.e. it now takes 10 turns longer on average until a granted gift request is forgotten.
    * Reduced the impact of Furious attitude on AI willingness to capitulate. (change 112b)
    * AI no longer refuses to capitulate when it thinks that continuing the war isn't in the enemy's interest. (May still refuse, but only for a few turns.)
    * War success factors into the comparison of vassal power with global average power, making the AI quicker to capitulate when losing badly.
    * Capitulated vassals are now Cautious toward all rivals (instead of sharing the master's attitude). (130v)
    * Vassals can no longer sign peace treaties by granting a gift to a human rival or asking for one.
    * No more oscillation of worst enemy (in the rare case) when the only disliked civs are fluctuating between Cautious and Annoyed. (130p)
    * Can no longer ask a civ to stop trading with one of its own vassals (change 130d).
    * Disabled change 130l b/c it came up too seldom. I.e. accepting an AI request no longer erases AI memory about a past rebuke of the same request, and a denied request no longer erases AI memory about past compliance. Can re-enable it through GlobalDefines.xml.
    * AI drafts fewer units (change 017, details in the manual).
    * Per-era modifier for King difficulty set to -3 as on Emperor (was -2 as on Monarch).
    * AI trade value for embargo adjusted; now more costly to get the AI to cancel OB while fighting any war (change 130f).
    * Fixed a crash in UWAI that could occur when voting on war through the Apostolic Palace.

commit d0a846bce6e73d5208181ba36db38f688a6a6467
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    v0.84: 2 serious bugs fixed
    * Bugfix concerning change 028 (submarines as escorts). The bug had given away the positions of foreign invisible units to the player by showing little flags on the map.
    * Crash in UWAI code fixed. Had been likely to happen after implementing a peace treaty by asking for free GPT.
    * Fixed an issue with the BtS AI: Units that had attacked on the previous turn were not counted for plot danger.

commit ccf5d7b95d5a7878f05f56e91ba8aac57a9599d2
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Apr 24 22:35:20 2017 +0200

    v0.83: 1 serious bug fixed in AI city evacuation
    
    * Fixed a bug that had caused the AI to always evacuate all but one defender from untenable cities instead of a random subset. Evacuation probability based on defensive modifiers now. (The 0.8 manual already said that modifiers were taken into account, but, apparently, I had forgotten to actually implement that part.) [advc.114a]
    
    * Improved the AI code for breaking naval blockades, and fixed a BBAI bug(?) that caused only some of the available ships to be counted. [advc.139].
    
    * Fixed a bug that caused population loss already on the second revolt (in cities that can't flip); should only happen on the third. [advc.099c]
    
    * Bugfix in AI code for balancing out trade offers. Previous fix turned out to be deficient.
    
    Minor tweaks:
    
    * AI civs now forget all "arrogant demands" when they declare any war. [advc.130o]
    
    * Health from Expansive trait shown in found button help text. [advc.004b]
    
    * Unrevealed cities now always shown as "Unknown" in Top 5; previously (BtS) shown by name if the owner was known. [advc.001d]
    
    New: Invisible units can get chosen as defenders when this protects visible units in the same tile. See change id 028 in the manual.

commit 0c3f38b7c28069235c400a36c8e4be2480741682
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Apr 21 14:37:48 2017 +0200

    v0.82: Minor tweaks, and two serious bugs fixed:
    
    * War evaluation cache now cleared between turns. Previously, an AI civ at war could remain unwilling to talk until a savegame was loaded (which clears the cache).
    
    * Fixed a bug that caused the DoW diplo penalty to be reduced upon making peace (which should only happen if war success was small or when vassals are involved). Also, the diplo penalty is now never reduced after wars in the Ancient era - attacks on Workers and Settlers need to have serious consequences.
    
    * In the early game, when tech and gold trading isn't possible, the AI makes peace for free with a human even if it thinks that the human is more eager to end the war.
    
    * Increased the impact of war success on the evaluation of lengthy wars.
    
    * The earlier fairness change (no early attacks on humans) no longer applies if a human has attacked the AI or its friends.
    
    * Increased a value that makes the AI inclined to continue war after bringing in help.
    
    * Reduced barb spawning when there are few tiles on which barbs could appear. Further reduced barb spawning on Tundra and Jungle.
